Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in ancient times "cure contuse," and what you do is to the patient who has this illness, make three cuts on his forehead; and let one of the cuts be as long as two thumbs all across the forehead going down until the nose, and the other two as two ribs above the temples, and beware of cutting the arteries that are beside the temples above the papery skin; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the length of three thumbs joined together; and have ready a piece of sponge and lots of cloths for wiping up the blood, then put in the spatula sharp on both sides as follows is its shape: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is beside the temple to the second incision; and scrape away all the flesh that is between the two cuts right down to the bone which lies under it; then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put the instrument which is called "cultellaire" into the first fissure and it is very sharp on one side, and blunt on the other, this is its shape: 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	Put the sharp side towards the flesh that is being cut, and the blunt side towards the bone, and push it in until it reaches the middle of the fissure. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the flesh so that the incision is continuous until it reaches what appears in the heart, and then similarly do in the middle fissure until the other defurcation; and then draw out the blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken; then put a tent of old cotton into each fissure, and put soft cloths soaked in wine and oil and vinegar on top, and keep it so that no boils arise; and on the third day untie the bandage, and administer a large poultice of hot water, then cure with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures with which one cures wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	Where the eyes are pricked 
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some catarrh comes accustomed, and you see the eyes tense and small, and weaken vision, and papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where one sweats in pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that these matters and this catarrh do not come only from many veins, and the mother cure that there is, if it is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you must order the patient to put his forehead behind, then make a great cut between the forehead, and another two finger widths away. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be until the bone; and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton, and linen tents; then bind over softened cloths in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until the flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying things, which cause flesh to grow. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and administer it in these wounds to generate flesh throughout. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	For the stuffing of ears  
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that is lodged in the ears is one of four things: either grains, or a beast, or a stone from a mine or similar things such as iron; or seeds, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing things such as water and easily flowing things and similar things.  
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When there is lodged in the ear a stone or another kind of thing that does not fit in the ear, nor grows in the ear, then put the ear to the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, and then administer extraction; and make him sneeze by condition, and hold his nostrils closed when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and elevate the ear upward. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes to fruition through this treatment; and if it does not come to fruition, you will administer an extraction with subtle forceps, of which the form is: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes to fruition with the forceps, that is good; if not, you will administer an extraction with a subtle lancet of small size; and if it does not come to fruition through this, you will make a cane of reed and insert the head of the cane or the hole of the ear firmly, and plug what is around the cane with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane; then treat it to come to fruition, for many times it comes to fruition as we have said; and if it does not come to fruition in any of these ways, you will take glue of which you take from birds, and put it on some instrument suitable for this, and place a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and treat it to come to fruition.  
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not leap from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear in this way as for an abscess that is hot it comes and spasms; and the manner of the incision is such that you make the patient healthy from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat or place depending; and let the incision be as a moon, until you reach the bone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it quickly at your mouth; and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is within and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin spatula subtly according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine pincers and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute pain then when a grain is in the ear it befits the patient to use sneezing as a first condition, and widely stuff the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And he should lie on that same ear where the pain is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out forcefully through this, it is good.  
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If this does not work, take many small stones according to the length of your thumb, light and warm them a bit by fire; then have the patient put one or two stones in his ear, and strike upon it from the other side with another stone; and do not cease to do this from stone to stone until the pain ceases entirely, and thus it will jump out entirely. And if you see that, take a piece of wire and push one end into the ear, and grasp the other end with fire so that the longest piece of wire burns; then repeat again with other pieces of wire until the pain ceases entirely, as we have said about stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of a creature, if it is of small size, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel it, then use extraction with pincers; and this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the removal of worms embedded in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not profit at all, then it is fitting that you look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms, remove them with fine pincers, and if you do not see any, take a cane of which this is the form: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the most delicate tip into the ear according to the amount of the patient's suffering, then gently pull out the whole cane; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, then plug around the bone with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out strong as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them or treat the distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which here is the form as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is of silver or iron, three nozzles below the small holes, and above a cover for distilling; and to press the distillation inside the instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point abundantly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines into the bone, and let the bone be in the ear; then put the razor inside all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or finished from the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be slightly warmed by the fire as they are distilled into the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of the ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have some opening in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults by stuffing a wound, or a splinter lodged inside the ear, and this stuffing sometimes comes entirely into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes the point appears through the opening, and one can see it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which then comes entirely in, if one cannot see it, is of grievous affliction in many conditions, and in this case it is fitting that you put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent stuffing, if the work has all these splinters, then this is its form. 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind entirely flat so that it does not hurt the ear; if the stuffing is a splinter or horn of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and pick it up lightly until all those splinters are removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is performed perfectly in the ear, then take a delicate razor and heat it slightly in the fire, then apply it to the body of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense the operation that the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce it lightly and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then put a tent into the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and powder it with ground vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, then it is fitting that you draw out the tent and insert another tent moistened with cerate which is made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, plunge a sponge and cloths in cold water and put them on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding, which are found in treatises on distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of paper 
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the remedy that comes to paper when they are moist and dry, it is fitting that you extend them with pliers and pincers, and the tip of a spatula from its roots; then put on the place powdered vitriol. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not come out, cauterize with a lentil-shaped cautery subtly, and cauterize again after the incision has healed; many times they recover, when nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return. 
de la gresle	of gravel 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there come to paper certain things that seem rough in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hailstone," and it is a gathering of large moisture on the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the hailstone moves from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know; do so with two large pincers, then lightly scrape each part, then take it with pincers, and cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it, then pierce a little of the paper; it does not matter to the patient; and if the fissure is large, stitch it together, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not exert force, for ointments will quickly restore it and engender flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone descends into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over and extend the hailstone with pincers, and cut it and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not matter; and when the hailstone is cut, wash the wound with sharp salt water, and treat the place so that it engenders flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is engendered in cloths of paper on top and this happens more to children than adults, and it grieves much their eyes
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel it moving among them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient puts his head on your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and arrange a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity it contains of exirnach from each part, and then put it on top; and press with your fingers on one side and the other so that the exirnach is gathered within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatu mile a trenchant a slit about as wide, and not larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and make the skin perfect until you reach the exirnach; and in several positions the exirnach comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat. 
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull it out then all at once with a piece of coarse cloth between your fingers in the direction outwards, and turn your hand to the right and left so that it is dispersed; and make sure you do not push into the slit, that you reach all the spatu mile up to the eye, that you do not hurt it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the arrowhead does not appear at the beginning of the incision, slightly widen the incision until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths with vinegar and water, and place them on the area, and bind securely. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt this remaining moisture. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil comes to the area, treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper 
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs grow old and are added to those that are natural, they harm them and cause various diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albugine, as long as it is a cause for their destruction; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is said in the chapter on cautery, or by incision and suture, or by cutting according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if you put a needle through all the thread on top; and let this be below the margin of the paper where the hairs grow below these hairs, and draw the thread over the top of all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs added, all along the spatula cutting, from the large tear duct to the small; then pull out the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then draw on the paper a figure of an anchor, as the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raised by the paper which is divided for all. 
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if anyone needs a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make at all the spatumile on the II lines that you have signed, and begin with the large tear to the small one; and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the lancet in one of the two angles of the heart, then flay it all; then bring together the two lips at a stitch with a needle with all the fine wool thread, and wipe the blood, and air out the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows at any sticky things, if you see fit to do this; and if not, don't care, then leave the stitch and the threads for III days or IIII; then treat the wound without stitches with drying and astringent things, because the paper will revive at the closing of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is useless (as the ancients said), and this work is done without fear; and if there is another way: it is that you sign the paper with a shape which is like the leaf of myrtle. 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then make sure he who holds it is equal to the small powers according to the form here: 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with thread, and put it in the shape; and put the other thread behind the large tear, and the second thread behind the small one, and assemble between your two hands the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have said, then assemble the two edges of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: then it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more skillful. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of canes is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and put the end inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two subtle ties as long as the paper and the width of a spatula is; and cut two ends into two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on that which rises from the oil of the paper, and strain the two canes from the two parts form; and leave it so for several days, and the leather that grows will be strained and healed and will carry, as long as it seeks by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the cut has some strength, then cure as long as it is healed; and when the wound grows closed, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer pull the hair; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you take a subtle needle, and you put a very fine silk thread through it; then assemble the pieces and tie each one subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange in the chase another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the heads of the two threads; then put the patient's head on your lap; and be below the sun so that the works are revealed, for it is a subtle and delicate work, then you put the needle all along the chase at the root of the hair adjacent, and make it pierce the paper hastily as you pull it over the natural hair; then you pull the hair up to the chase, and you put in the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out all along the chase in the paper with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the flesh is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will treat the flesh underneath along the entire thread that you have ordered, until the flesh comes out freely through the holes above it and you see it with the vision of the eye; then you will treat the flesh and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh grows up over it; and if the hairs are small, you will accompany one long hair from a horse's tail, and let it grow with the one that you are letting go of, until it is elongated and then remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rotting of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacratio" or rot comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by incision of a wound, or by cutting or by cautery, and by similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work is that you cleave that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put flax tents inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not right that you use in its treatment things that dry and constrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose water or elderflower water and flaxseed boiled together, and ointments of diascordium melted in any of the oils, and wrap a tent, and cure it with that. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal according to the form that it was before; and this work that we have said is no more than directions for this illness, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh that comes to the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which is truly called "axacrati," is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cause comes from wounds and fissures and cautery and similar things; and the way to perform the procedure is that you take a needle, in which it has a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then spread the flesh above the entire needle, and cut at one-sixth of an inch wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is fitting, that is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two fissures on either side within the paper; and let the sides of the two fissures be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has no "Greek I"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are below, from that which surrounds the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then apply the cure that we have said of softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.  
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a split or a stitch or a cautery, it is necessary that you make a full split below the hairs of the skin, and according to what has been said before; then sever between the two edges of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters prepare all sorts of things so they can bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what suits him of work and instruments has many dispositions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	From beneath the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in a man's hand in such a way that the skin above is sewn with the white of an egg, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor beneath the skin and lift it up; and hold it with pincers, as long as you cut what is joined by a subtle spatula, which is not too sharp nor too blunt so that the patient does not suffer that the spatula is too sharp or that the eye blurs; and let your incision, by which you separate that which is assembled, be light, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and heal all that which is joined, and do it sometimes with salt water in the eye, and lift with sweet water and colophony; then put between the skin and the eye a linen tent, and put wool soaked in plenty of egg white on top of the eye; and after the third day use colophony and soothing things as long as it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the angle of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and resembling hard flesh; and another which is not nervous, but resembles white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and considered as pincers, cannot be grasped; and both resemblances begin towards the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all the sight and all the light and movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is such that the patient puts his head in good health, then he opens his eyes; and lifts the paper to your hand, then coils the nail like pincers of small doubleure, and extends it above; then takes a needle, and puts horsehair, or cowhair, or oxhair, and strong thread; and doubles the point of the needle a little and inserts it into the nail, and pierces it through with the whole needle, and binds the nail with a thread and extends it above, and flays all the hair on the side of the nail which follows the prunele and silk to the hair up to the head, then cuts the remainder at the root of the tear duct with the whole spatumile subtly and with small force, and leaves the flesh natural or tear duct, so that by incision no body of tears usually comes; and sometimes only bind the nail to the oncine alone, and to the thread, as we have said; then flay one has all the spatumile according to which the form is.  
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure that the spatula does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the eye is not pierced; and after the incision pour into the eye a bit of silk thread, and with a collar made of silver, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, many times this kind of nail is cured by medicines; and it grows back as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, operate on the eye of the patient, and take a small sharp spatula according to this form:  
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail subtly, and if you see that it diminishes a little and the rasping hastens it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of silver and a red collar and silk thread, and cover the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the tear duct harms the eye greatly, then suspend it to a string and cut off a portion, not entirely, so that tears cannot come through; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the iris 
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eye of some men, flesh sometimes grows, covering the iris and clinging to the eyelids, turning red like a rose of balauste; the work is such that the patient puts his head in good health, then he cuts the flesh and removes all that flesh with appropriate forceps for this purpose, and holds it firm; then he cuts the first piece of flesh and continues cutting with a razor until the end, taking care not to injure the eye during the operation; let the incision be made on the spatula as we have said in the incision of the inguinal hernia and with the small forces with which one removes the sebaceous gland, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of wormwood bruised or distill into it red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines; then put hot cotton on the eye with an egg white so that it is assured against a hot abscess; and if anything remains and the pus overcomes you and you doubt a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and do this as long as there is flesh attached in the eye by this likeness.  
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you alleviate the treatment of each one who is weak from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb can endure that work. 
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	They are red veins that are covered over the eye, and steal from sight its work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary then in the first place that you look at whether the eye is where it is strong, and there is no other disease except for the redness; then proceed in this way: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins at all the incisions according to your knowledge, and let the incisions be subtle double according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be given in degrees within the body according to this form: 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then one must carefully cut those veins subtly and wipe the blood hour after hour until you see those veins far from the eye; and be careful not to pierce the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun and be very ardent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, then distill green and red coliere into the eye to corrupt what remains hidden. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot gather all of that in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of soothing things to ease the pain of those veins, and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and there is assurance of a hot abscess, then begin again according to the manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	They are called "arissati" fistulas: when you treat it with a cautery and burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then incise upon the abscess where it should flow, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then shape all the instruments according to this form; it is called "aspre chief," and is made of hard iron at the head end, and pointed like a file as it is in the present form. 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Place it upon the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a bit until you know that the corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the site with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the fistula is sewn together and flesh grows and the body of the fistula is sewn together and remains so for 40 days, and it does not reopen and is not abscessed and no bad things happen, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, there is nothing else to do but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take a drill according to this form, and let the head of the drill have 3 angles, and let the drill be thinned down to its point as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye one inch, then turn the drill entirely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels this because the vein in this will tell if they are holding their hand on their nose; and then restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the wound, the matter will go to the nose; which is a lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	From the removal of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is completely open and there is neither clouding nor diminishing, it is necessary that you bind the patient; then apply a bandage, then put on cupping glasses or cauterize without injuring to suck, then place on the eye a plaster made of acacia and aloe and frankincense and sarcocol, and then strain the eye, and cover it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each into four, and then put one upon the other according to the quantity that the eye may need; then bind it above with a hard bandage, and begin again the cupping glasses to suck without injuring; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the strained eye day and night, and if the bandages become loosened, it is necessary that you strain them very much; then remove the bandage after day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, it is good; if not, begin again the plaster and the cloths and the bandage and the cupping glasses until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Where a rupture of cloth has occurred
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a rupture comes in the cloth weave, then it appears, and there are strips of paper like resin grains, and it is easy to see; then if you have seen it torn, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then thrust another needle where the doubled thread of the tear is located; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to its position; then grasp the place of the doubled thread and tie one part of the weave around it, and pull it tight, then remove the needle and put a softened wool cloth soaked in abundance of egg white on it; and leave it as long as the threads knit with the weave, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and often the wound is restrained by the weave on each side of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a large appearance, pierce it with a delicate scalpel that comes perfectly straight from the point, and drain the whitish moisture and reduce the swelling, and then extract it when it is healed. 
de la bowe de l’oil	from the belly of the eye 
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a belly which is assembled in the eye, appearing like sharp descending, and it is not sharp; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on an appropriate and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it as much as you see the belly coming up over your eyes; then let it be attached, and do not descend and let the light be obscured, and see the patient things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is sharp, and if the descending of the belly is not even as we have said.  
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a subtle spatula and place it on the cornea cloth, prick through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea cloth, as long as the pus comes out; and when it has come out, distill into the hot sharp oil mixed with honey, or sharp oil or fenugreek boiled and honey, then let it be cured by another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the sharp oil 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the resemblances of the sharps in the division, and what it is necessary for piercing; so work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, far from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of oil in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument beside the cornea by the thickness of a ray in that whiteness of the eye to the part of the lesser tear duct, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda way be at the perfection of the measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the cornea cloth, then put the instrument up to where the sharp point is, then express it below one way after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it is sharp now, let the patient see it in front of him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the point rises again the second time, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not rise, carefully extract the almond by turning your hand bit by bit; then put it back in a sharp point of a gem seed, and lift the eye from within. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put the eye with wadding soaked in rose oil and a lot of egg yolk, and bind it with the healthy eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Nowadays, we and those of our time put on common broth with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have eyes too hard, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which has this form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle place, then put in almond, as we have said;
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, untie the eye bandage before the seventh day and apply a dressing for abscesses; and when it is appeased, remove the bandage and put a strip of linen on its face to cover it for a few days, and keep it in a darkened room thereafter. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then gradually leave the house little by little and return to normal activities; and know that no disciples should interfere in this matter. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	One man came to us who was from the Yrach, and he told us that in his country they made a kind of almond paste with which one sucked the water, but I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new invention. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almond paste so that those who do not know them can recognize them: and they should be made purely of grain. 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of those of this same subtlety, and the last in III sharp angles. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh off the nose 
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or noses growths diverse, of which there are some that resemble scorpions with many feet; and if there are such growths with flesh tinged with a fox color, and if there is flesh soft of good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that one therefore of those growths which is soft and not tinged, it behooves that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and work his nostrils, and pour oil on those growths, and draw them forth; then cut off what you can hold with a delicate sharp spatula on one side, as much as you know that growth is all removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that one cannot cut off, work it with all the delicate instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if without swelling or abscess rises, cut as it behooves; and if they are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the flesh is scorched and all the growths are removed, then pour on the nose fresh and sharp wine. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the newborn child works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh on the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then it behooves you to put a flax thread a little thick, and knotted by hand, with a space of one inch or less between each knot; and place the child's cheek upon the thread in its nostril, and pull in odorant until it comes through the nostril into the mouth; and often children are done thus at schools, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them one after the other as we are who are on the thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as much as you know that the new flesh has corrupted the other flesh, then treat the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and return it to its original place as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put on the nose a cane of lead for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, into which one distills oils and medicines onto the nose:  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and conduct it in the same way; and if you see fit, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have a handle at the top to hold it while heating the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh out of the nose 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" is born from the head near the nose and grows and becomes large until it is seen as a thing to behold; and for this reason it behoves you to cut it at the beginning, and remove all the bone, then put on its place a cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it while it is large, take heed if it is hard, of red color, of poor sense: if not touch it with iron for it is an ulcerated abscess, for when it is cut, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of red color, and you see that it can be all cut out, then empty the patient and cut without fear and cure the place with drying and restraining things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilage works, it profits little, except in some men.
