Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore when this happens to anyone, if he looks at whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then he joins the two lips together with a suture, then cures it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you flay all the parts of their core so that they bleed, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and extract them, and powder with powdered dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put on the powders a piece of plaster of Paris or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it drains by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is such that you bring together the wound: either with needles, as we have said in sewing of the belly; or with thread, as I have taught you. 
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes within the lips occur abscesses hard, resembling grains of millet, both smaller and larger; then it is fitting that you turn back the lips, and cleave upon each nodule, and take them with pincers and cut in two parts; then apply the lye after incision with powdered vitriol until the blood has been dried up; and then olive oil, and heal the wound with dry things until it is healed. 
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums 
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there arises upon the gums flesh overgrown, which the ancients called “albulus”; it is fitting that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood flow out; then apply powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders upon the wound; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of the deaf 
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, crusts which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and citron-colored and worm-eaten, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your lap, and raise the teeth or the crusts that appear, as much as there is nothing left; and do the same with blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other blemishes, as long as they are cleansed; and if one removes what was at first cause, it is good; if not, one begins again the second day and the third, until you have raised everything; and know that teeth need different forms of instruments to raise, according to what the work shows, for the razor with which one raises broken teeth has other forms than those with which one raises between the teeth; and these forms and others be prepared with you. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay as much as you can in pulling it, for this one must not do; because it is a very high substance so that one has no excuse for pulling it. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to pull, it is necessary that you are certain of the aching tooth. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks it is in a sound tooth, and pulls out the good tooth; and nevertheless the pain does not depart because of this, as long as the bad one remains, for we have often wanted to do this with these healers; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you flay around the tooth at all its edges very strongly to preserve the gum from all sides; then pull it with your fingers or with subtle forceps at the first stroke and stroke, as long as it is well loosened, then firmly grasp the forceps; and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.  
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take any of these instruments and insert its tip into each side lightly, and move it as you did first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and decayed, it is necessary that you fill it with cloths where the holes are; and if you extract it subtly with pincers so that it does not break when extracting; and it is very wise to work around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and leave a part remaining, and return to the patient because of the malice of the root causing greater pain than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to do as ignorant barbers often do, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth, and do not apply what we have said; but they cause great illness by the roots that remain, or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply ground vitriol to the place; and if this does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one pulls out teeth first should have long points and thick handles so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; these are their shapes: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick limbs so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be of well-made iron, and they should have teeth to hold the flesh. 
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, it is fitting that you put on the place cotton moistened with butter for one or two days. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the flesh is softened, then you put in the forceps which are called “algefri”, whose head resembles a bird's beak; and they are made inside like a file and this is their shape: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is fitting that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called “althali”, that is to say, a small spatula, of which this is the shape: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it must be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps because of this, it is good; if not, you must help yourself with all the instruments, from which the forms come here after: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument that has two jaws, of which here is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other ironworks which are in front in the manner of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tongs, of which here is the form: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument must be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments with teeth exist; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise master artificers invent by themselves their instrument according to what their works and the illness demonstrate to them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of others, so that it does not break the chariot or other bones, or it rots, if he seeks the instruments that suit him, as I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which here is the form:  
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, if you have all these instruments: 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural course of the body, and the form is ugly, even in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth was born after the dentition, and is not in its proper place, and it cannot be treated or filed; then the rasp; and if it is connected with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is shown, and which resembles a small beak, and is made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the rasp bit by bit in small portions for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is visible so that it can be filed, then use a file with one edge as its shape is shown here. 
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth little by little in gentle strokes, so that it does not move while it enters; then smooth the surface at the end with no rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then file down its sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not cut the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth falls out 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth falls out, whether by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on what he chews without pain, and you have treated it with astringent medicines, and that does not work; then you must restrain it with a thread of gold, for a silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the crooked teeth, if there is one or several, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again until the part where you began, and pull your hand subtly and gently, so that it does not move; and let your ligation be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the head of the bone with forceps and assemble them and put them back between the healthy teeth so that it does not bite the tongue; then leave it so tight as long as it can stay and if it loosens or the threads break, remove it with another thread; if it remains and serves thus for its entire time, this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two broken ones as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the head of the tooth is removed, we put it back in its place again and again as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes make a form of a cow's bone tooth and put it in the place where there is a deficiency, and remove it as we have said, and it will remain and serve for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the ligament of the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament which comes below the tongue by nature, or one is born with it; or by accident of a sewn wound; and the operation is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your lap, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, as long as the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is from sewing of a wound, then put in the hook and cut the ligament widely; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery which is below; and when you have done this, lift the area with sharp rose water and alum, or sharp cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and bind the patient each night, so that the wound may not close. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if a flow of blood comes, put ground vitriol on the spot; and if it does not stop, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for that; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of a dark color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it leans towards whiteness, and there is moisture, then cut the skin, and make an incision with a fine scalpel, and free it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding does not stop in your work, put ground vitriol on it until it is quenched, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the pus; then lift the place from dirt and salt, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes boils come inside the throat which are called "godath", and we properly call them the two tonsils, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the flow of blood; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will cut it, or it will burst on its own; and if it is of a whitish color and the root is fine, have your instrument ready to cut, but look first to see if the abscess is hot, at rest and appeased.  
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his back to your left side, and open the mouth and grasp the tonsil with your hands, and press the tongue down below all of the instrument, so it is shaped; and it should be silver or fine steel as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue against all these instruments, and you see the abscess, take the lancet and put it into the almond, and hold it firmly on top as much as you can; and don't pull anything away from the cloths, then apply a bandage to the instrument, so that it has a shape which resembles strength; nevertheless, the heads are bent, and one against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of hard iron or steel. 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, take the forceps, which are shaped like this:  
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And they are sharp on one side, and blunt on the other; and when you have grasped one of the almonds, grasp the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water that is both hot and easy to swallow. And if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with hot water in which pomegranate rinds have been cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood has stopped; then treat it until it is healed; and if at any time other abscesses develop in the throat besides the two almonds, cut them as you did the two almonds previously. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, to be known the abscess of small sense; and it had almost completely closed off the entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she remained like that for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had forced two reins through the two holes where it was born. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then and put one lancet in one hole, then I drew it out forcefully and drew a large portion of pus; then I did the same thing through the other hole where it was born, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that I put the lancet into the abscess and removed some of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the passage of the throat was unblocked for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess would grow back again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, so that it became very large; then I lanced it and cauterized it inside the throat; thus it stopped growing; and I departed from those parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterward. 
de l’uve	from the eye 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When a cold descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below large and round, it is called "eye." 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, and you see that the pus of the abscess has subsided, and it is subtle, it behoves you to cut it; and that which is round and gathered and is not long; and it is bloody or a yellowish color or black, it behoves you to make an incision. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It behoves you, then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, from its whiteness and length, to make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before; then insert the lancet into the eye, and draw it underneath, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned for the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is fitting that you do not cut away more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut away more, it grieves the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and heal it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid to be cut, it is fitting that you use something for the cauterization of his fearful senses. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and pointed. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your sound hand, and then presses his tongue to the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and configures it with a sharp, living point, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and in employing the end of this instrument, of which here is the form:  
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And say that if a head is covered with hair where the medicine is to be applied, like the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument all over the medicine on the eye; and the patient shall lie on his side so that saliva and mucus flows from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend into the throat, and the blepharitis; then hold your hand all over the medicine and press it upon the eye, for a quantity of half an hour, until you see it become numb and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see this, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument into all the cotton on the cane above it, until the cotton is heated upon the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and let the scab fall off after four days or five. And if you need to begin the cautery again from the medicine, then begin again, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse that which is around the medicine; and let him be washed with cold water, and let him be treated with gargles until he is healed.  
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamus and wormwood and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them into a pot, and add water and boil; and let the pot be well sealed with strong earth, and halfway up the pot insert an instrument shaped as follows: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or iron, and one end should be inserted into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through a tube until the eye is mortified; then repeat often until the eye dries up, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do this except when a hot abscess is declining. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside the head a quail egg, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for a quail egg does not make the vapor heavy on the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether safe. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fishbone, or something else gets stuck in the throat; so it is fitting that you draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move; and what does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, it is fitting that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps it will release the stuck thing through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of stale bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will come out, and then draw it out forcefully; and if it does not come out forcefully from what we have said, take an instrument of plumb according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and have the head raised up high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all life leave him, nor push any bone inside; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows where the thing is airy; if he swallows down, or he draws it back forcefully with the whole instrument equally, until it is drawn out. 
de la sansue de la gorge	from the mucous of the throat 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is the mucous, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not profit at all, then look into the throat of the patient toward the sun, then press his tongue against the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the mucous, draw it out entirely with a small hook, or with subtle forceps that are good for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a cane with a pointed end, and put it in the throat of the patient, then put the hot point of the iron on the cane and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a sharp pain every day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and make it swallow, moving it in their hand often; and as soon as they feel the pain, they will spit. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if they do not spit as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I described in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way to fumigate is that you take a pot with live coals, and cover it with a cloth pierced in the middle, and put the head of the instrument into the hole. Then you pour your fumigation, and have the patient put the end of the cane into their mouth, closing their mouth so that the smoke does not escape but reaches the throat; and the throat will now fall away, and if it does not spit, then start the fumigation again many times; let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and such, and do not drink water; then they will need to spit out by this means.  
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the sinus, if it can be seen, resembles curved tongs for entering the throat; and it has the appearance of a sewing needle's beak, and it has roughness like a file so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; see here its form: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses 
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses are similar according to what memory comes here after one another in this book and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways of which one is in its own likeness and from the moisture that it holds. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is according to the places where they are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the buttocks, and abscesses in fleshy places are different from those that come at joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.  
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one must not pierce, as long as the belly is ripening according to its fulfillment; and if to such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, as with abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it as long as it is ripe around, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal limb; or where it is near the fundament, pierce it even when it is not ripe; and it is not fitting that you pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for that which is near the fundament, so that it may ripen perfectly, and be elongated within, and there come a fistula; and it cannot heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is fitting that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is fitting that you make the perforation where the pus most collects in the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the perforation be long with the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all its equal parts where there is no weeping. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that weep, according to that member. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is worth noting that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front of them, the body will be elongated by its venom, and is full of a lot of filth; and perhaps the lips and depths harden. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what its limbs need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you administer small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover; when it has become yellow as drapelz, and is numb, then it is necessary to do as one does for buboes: and if there are some that are split into three angles, and some that you cut like a myrtle leaf, as abscesses of angers; and if there are some where you make a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts.  
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, like a superficial abscess, it is fitting that you pierce it thoroughly; and it is fitting that when the abscess is large, and it has collected great pus, and you pierce it, you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; then stopper the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing further; do this many times in succession, until all the pus is gone; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes leaps with the discharge of pus, and by chance the patient dies, and you are not to blame. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound clean, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a full incision, apply strips of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many holes, you should place a strip in each one so that they come together against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the flesh, and you have sewn it around, then fill it with old cotton or shavings of flax linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then unbind it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water quickly and easily, moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding continues, apply a bandage and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book to the wound; and if it is during winter, and the wound or abscess is very nervous, you should put cloths soaked in wine and warm oil on it; and if it is summer, and the wound is fleshy, you should put cloths soaked in cold water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, for three days, as we have said; then untie the abscess, wipe it, and treat it as appropriate until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this should be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter. 
des soros	of serpents 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the core of a boil comes small abscesses, and are manners of us that are in cloths, as the joiner of a hinge, and much there are of resemblances.  
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some of fat and such where there is moisture as well as pulsations; and if there are such that are hard and piercing at the waist, and there is no doubt whether the artery does contrary.  
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist so it is that you try with all the instrument which is called "introducer", from which the form comes here after, what it contains.  
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so let it pass over for a long time. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, so flay without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it returns then when you leave something; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave until the next day; and this will run what remains in the night. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then start the cotton again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain overnight; then heal the wound with ointment suitable for it, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds thick pus, do it according to this form, for a long time; and scrape your ointments, and flay it from all sides, and put all your treatment of drawing away the pus where it lies; and if the artery makes you contrary, do what I have told you afterwards. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for an abscess if it is pierced, and in the loins and in the groin as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the lancing on a pierced abscess and moistened, is lighter, for they are points of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or head where it has no moisture, and of those were the abscesses that I cut or head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if one had done any, he would have made as good a wound as from a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	For other abscesses coming or chief, those which come as chief of children and as roots of ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that the pus can come out; and treat it as it is necessary. 
des scrophules	Of scrofula.  
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses happen at the neck, and below the armpits, and in the groin, and rarely they come elsewhere on the body, and they are many, and joined together with each other. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own bone, as the knot and the abscess on the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofula are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones which do not want to obey health.  
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then which you see of good disposition to be touched, and it seems the color of the body, and moves at every part and is not near to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the duct, and is not deep; it is fitting that you cut it above, and scrape it from every part, and extend the two lips of the wound with a needle, if you need it, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and let the instrument not be sharp nor cutting so that the hands do not slip, and do not go too far forward lest you cut what you should not.   
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that stanch blood, and remove the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work until you complete it; then look with your index finger to see if any small scrofula remain, and cut them out and clean them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not right to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then bandage it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you know how to cut the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofula that have excess, pierce them where it appears dead; and pierce it as the one previously mentioned, hanging down, then apply tents with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, apply ointment dressing promoting flesh until it is healed. 
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have strabismus, it is necessary that the fold of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be scraped; and this should not be done by anyone, for all the veins and the lung of the patient are affected in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two tonsils. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the canal of the lung, it is necessary to scrape the epiglottis to avoid the loss which comes from strangulation.  
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to split the epiglottis, we should split it below three or four circles with a small incision across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the incision in the soft palate, not in the cartilage; and those who are skilled in the sectioning of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough to be avoided. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to the whole width, then split the chest until it reaches the windpipe; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the diaphragm, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the sectioning of the phlegm of the windpipe which escapes through the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed when we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the chest, and sew it all alone without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote flesh growth, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely opened, and the patient is judged to be dead, and his breath fails. 
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and because the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and cleanse it, as long as it was cleansed; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a maiden took a knife and stuck it in her throat and cut part of the channels of the pharynx; and I was called to cleanse her, and I found her as if dead.  
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come from it, and although she had not covered her vein nor conducted anything but the throat, and the veins were cut by the wound. 
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound and treated it until it was healed; and nothing further happened to the young woman except that her voice became hoarse, and then returned to normal afterward; therefore I say that one should not be afraid in cutting the epiglottis. 
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess colored like yellow wax, and is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; when natural there is no cause.  
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental cause occurs in two ways, one of which resembles a fatty growth, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from a blood vessel; there is danger involved, and it is not fitting to work with fire except on those that are small, and thoroughly probe and examine all the surrounding area: if you find it as soft as new fat and it does not adhere to any vein, cut it out as one cuts out a growth and treat it in its entirety, if there is any; and bind it well at first, and treat it as appropriate until it is perfectly healed.  
des nous	of us 
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are for us, of which I will say all the resemblances; and now it is fitting that I say all the difference that is between us and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that fever is heat and lasting fever, as long as the ebullitions have not passed, and putrefaction is accomplished; then the fever and heat subside.  
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With swelling there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a bruise, and becomes large; and they are according to two resemblances, either fatty or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.  
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is fitting, when you come to the treatment of swelling, that you try and inquire first with all the instruments called "introducer," according to what its form will be or chapter which comes after. 
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire into abscesses of us is that you take or a moister place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then let it be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intruder, and take care lest it jump out. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs quickly, whatever color it has, do as I have said of the other abscesses; and if after the intruder no moisture comes, know that it is greasy, so make a cross, and take it with pincers, and lightly scrape it from each side, and guard the place where it lies so that you draw it out cleanly with the new; and if you cannot draw it out cleanly, draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains nothing, the nose returns many times; and if there remains a bit of it, and it does not grieve you, apply the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, extract the wound, and put soothing things on hot abscesses, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the nose is large, cut the two edges of the wound, and cure it with those who bring flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or another hastens and apply the place of ground vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound rots, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to cutting what remains in the nose. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of introducer instruments, and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three ways: large, medium, and small, to enclose the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like the needles with which we sew up the sores, and are made of citrine iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more, and are more tried with black lead for enclosing the curves of a fistula; and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of lancets are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are lancets that have two curves in three ways; and there are lancets that have three curves, and are also of three ways; and there are lancets that have two curves, and lancets with only one curve, and are also of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these, which are made for cutting, and there are some that do not cut any stronger than from one side, with which one strips the veins, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and among these instruments are the lamels inserted in handles, so that the patient does not notice them when opening abscesses; and they are of three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use any stronger than in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar parts; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a fistula knife, according to this shape, with which one drains blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And put it back in place several times according to the alignment of the veins, and arteries, and never according to this great form: 
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them must proceed according to this form from line b. to line g.: 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine made from charcoal, then bring the two edges of the wound together with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down and is softened because of its size as it happens in women, then cut it into two ribs above, by two similar incisions; so that one holds onto the other at the end of the one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from line b. up to line g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and do what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever else is necessary in the treatment until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the runoff of blood, then you must fill the wound with softened cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it removes the remainder and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits 
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.: 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with appropriate ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofula, then cut it as we have said when cutting scrofula, and if the wound runs pus, then apply a cautery as we have said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery
