Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is severed and the skin above it is stitched, many times abscesses form, and the same thing happens to an engorged vein with an abscess; and if you know when it is due to the artery, the abscess will be long and slender; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel something pulling away; and when it is from the vein, it appears round and smooth; and it is folly to open this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and at the angles or the neck and in many other places, and it is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore it is necessary to avoid using cautery, and the one who is in charge must also avoid it; and in the case of swelling due to a severed artery, make a long incision through the skin above it; then operate as for ligatures, separating the artery from the surrounding tissues until it is exposed; then insert a needle beneath it and pass it through to the other side, drawing out the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries located in the temples; then prick the area between the two ligatures with a surgical instrument until all the pus that is there comes out, and the abscess will be released; then apply a bandage impregnated with oil, until the ligatures close; and treat it with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to vein engorgement, you must hold in your hand whatever part of the abscess adheres to the skin, then insert a needle under the spot that you are holding, and pass it through, threading it with a double thread so that you can draw it out from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have told you, making a ligature on one or both ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads will come loose, insert another needle through all the threads under the entire abscess to the incision of the first needle, and draw out the threads in four places; then open the abscess until the excess pus comes out, then cut away the excess tissue and leave what is ligated; then place a softened cloth bandage soaked in wine and oil, and apply bandages and ointments as necessary until it is healed.  
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves 
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or by too much labor, and similar things. 
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and arms and all their joints where they are, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in several positions without pain; and when it is removed, the patient feels pain, and it is not completely part of the body, but below the heart; and moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and the one that is in the joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would contract; and the one that is on the head or forehead, makes the skin swell. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a lancet, and flay it, then the bone setter assembles the wound with stitches, and cares for it until it is healed.  
des grosses boces pendans	Large boils hanging 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the bellies and nowhere else a swelling, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots, and thick flesh; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had tiny roots, and they were easily cut, and constantly oozed moisture. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found that one weighed eighteen ounces and the other six ounces, and the operation is such that if you look, the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist and has subtle roots; if you cut with a scalpel wide and have the fire cautery in your presence. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist there often comes excessive blood flow, and if the vein does not stop bleeding, then you must use the cautery; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision with iron, then take a thread well-made from flax, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then loosen it, and do not cease to tighten the flax thread until it stops the artery, and bleeds through it without effort; and if the roots are large, then be afraid to cut them immediately because of the belly, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize it so that it does not grow back; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tendon which is of a dark color and poor in sense and full of milky appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers later.  
quant li boude ist fuer	When the arm is strong 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the arm comes by cautery of wound or fissure of sinew, and it is on the belly and in this some of the bowels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood which cuts from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it is by the rupture of the sinew and by the issue of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and appears with diverse issue.  
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its two ends it responds, and then returns, and by chance if it is constricted, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for great effort. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is from moisture, it is a light thing, and appears well when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrict at all; and if it is from blood, then it appears by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is from windiness, it is soft to touch, and the work is such that you look to see if the appearance is from the blood of the artery, or the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, it is necessary that you order the patient to hold his belly, and be extended all straight, then sign around the whole abdomen with chalk; then command him to grasp often between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed at every span, then extend half of the abscess above at the end of a large needle; then tie it around with a strong thread or a cord of very strong silk firmly, and let the knot be loose; then work on half the extended abscess above the tie, and put your index finger, and grasp the intestine; if you find it caught in the tie, untie it, and push the intestine out from the belly; and if you find the bowel, grasp it with the needle, and cut off the excess; and if the artery opposes you, or the vein, go well around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape that you make pierce; then pull the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it dries up, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or cut it off when it becomes subtle and rotten, then cure what is necessary, and sew the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place with what is necessary, and suture the place. 
dou chancre	a sore 
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of a sore, and how one should work upon it with medicines, and how one should avoid the treatment with iron; and we say that a sore grows in the flesh, and great caution is needed in its cure, and the ancients said that when a sore is in a place where it can be shaved, such as a sore which is on the breasts, and on the thighs, and in similar places, then one should remove it all when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not right for you to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone ever healed any before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him fast if he has manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good place to do the work; then cut your oncines or sore and the hair from all sides, and bone from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood run out completely, and wipe the place well with your hand or with something else, and if the running of blood prevents you from cutting into the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is eclites only; and one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: to wit, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you give medicine to this resemblance of dropsy which is called “eclites” by medicine, and the cure does not profit, then consider whether the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things; if so, do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient is of strong constitution, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed thus: lay the patient straight upon your hands, and have the attendants press the belly at the end by pushing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the spatumile espinous according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on two sides. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let it have a point, and in no way be so deep that it can reach the intestines when inserted, nor pierce them; then see if the dropsy is directed toward the intestines: if so, you must cleave beneath the navel three finger-widths to the right above the hipbone; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision will be on the left of the navel three finger-widths; and if it is for the spleen, let it be on the right, and do not allow the patient to lie upon the incision lest the superfluities run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it in, and lift your hand along the entire spatula between the skin and the flesh as when flaying to the amount of a fingernail or so around; then pierce the flesh until the spatula comes to its eighth place, and this is the place of the acute angle, then draw it out, and push this instrument into which shape: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a subtle silver cane, and is of iron or of light artichoke, and has in the lower part a small hole; and on one side, III holes; and II on the other, and I on the other; and the head is cut like a quill pen, and this is the form of the incision which scribes use to cut their quills: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it descends now onto the instrument; empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than what is right in that hour, by chance the patient might die because of the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or his jaw might become numb, or he might approach death; but empty according to the quantity of his strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength signify, and his pulse; then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held for the heart which pierces the hole that is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then start the instrument again the next day if you see the patient suffering thus, and treat the point a small quantity; do this every day, and be careful not to force as long as there remains but a point. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and leave a great deal of fluid there, then treat the area with dry earth or hot sand, and through much sweating or bathing in the sun; let him drink it; and use drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the fluid, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the constriction of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary soon, he should pierce all the way through with a very fine tool according to this form:  
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place a small tube of lead inside, bind it and leave it in place for three or four days. When he wants to urinate, remove the tube so he can urinate and then replace it; and by chance if it is not necessary, because the urine which comes will not let it close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose pores are small, if they are treated with a clove of garlic, as we have said, will widen. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have their pores in place are blemished, for none are born who have the pores at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upward; and they cannot engender because the matter cannot come up to the marrow, and it is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of working is that the patient lies often on his back, then stretches the head of the penis and cuts it as the size of a feather so that the pores are in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which often occurs, and if it happens, have it stopped by someone who stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these pustules come to the penis and are an ugly sore appearance; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it is necessary that you grasp them with a fine lancet, and cut and cleanse them all, then put softened cotton on Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the pustule is malignant, of foul color and discharging, it is necessary that you administer a cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the pustule is at the top of the penis and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the pustule which is inside first; and when it is removed, then you cure the one outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cure them together, unless the flesh of the penis is well secured so that it is not pierced, blackness and corruption come to its penis and testicles; so it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then bind an ointment plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate rind and vinegar on top, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a discharge of blood comes, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help in two ways together: that is to say, in the discharge of blood and in corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you draw or conduct from the penis a cane of lead, and make the patient urinate among them; and when the hair burns at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, then you must scorch it with the chosen instrument, so that the ligatures are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if it is a grievous thing to devise this, it is necessary that you scorch it at the spathula any spot on the head of the penis and the skin; then separate well between them, and put a delicate linen cloth moistened in cold water so that it does not burn immediately. 
de la circoncision	Of circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a matter of simple continuation like other wounds; nevertheless, when we undertake this task willingly, especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the lightest for safety. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have gained through experience. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions use an entire knife, and with force, and at one go; the heart was cut out because there are two layers, and by chance if one cuts above it, the one below remains. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it is necessary to cut again, and the pain is doubled, and with cleaning which is done in one go, the tip of the member is not well assured; and with the cleaning of the foreskin, the iron may slip by chance, ruining the work, and many times they are born without needing cleaning and I have seen it. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification which is made to all the length of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut evenly both above and below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, if you cut evenly in I all the while you hold it; but let the thread be well twisted around the leather; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if they understand, that you are only making them tie the thread around the penis just so, and then let them play in all ways that you can; then let them come between your hands straight, and put the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the children do not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the penis and blow on it or breathe on it, and draw it up as high as the head of the penis is in; then clean it well of the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the marked place with a double thread, then tie it under the other tie; and hold it with two fingers by the second ligature to the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the two ties, then quickly remove the heart from above and draw the head of the penis; then let the blood run little by little, for that is the cure; and put powder on it and on the powder a bandage glued with half an egg cooked with rose water tempered with good fresh rosemary oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it is healed.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for purification is this: the two jaws should be held and sharp, and the jaws should also be as large as the handle equally. 
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the kernels inside flee at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your knuckle, just as the leus face abscesses; and the cup equally, and if you cannot hold it to your knuckle, take it with tongs, and then cut. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass III days, and what is below the rod is swollen, leave it until the abscess underneath is soothed, and lightly scar it; if you can cut it, then guard yourself from the part of the rod, for it will not harm anything. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal then the place of things within the wound with powder, as we have said in treating powders, and if you cut too deep into the kernel, and it goes above, it will not harm anything; heal it then, as we have said, until it is healthy. 
dou retenement de l’urine	regarding retention of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or frozen blood, or a bowel, or a tumor, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone which is at the neck of the bladder, it is fitting that the patient be bent on his knees; and his feet be placed on his back, and he extend his belly above his back, and restrain the patient from stretching as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder will be forced towards the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is fitting that you administer extraction with an instrument called a "syringe", which has this form: it should be made of thin silver, light and smooth like a bird's feather; and the tube should be a palm and a half long, and thin at the tip.  
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of extracting urine is such that you take a double thread and tie its head to a piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess of the wool and push it up to the head of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and lukewarm water.
des maladies de la vessie	of the illnesses of the bladder 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see sharp waters and medicines distilled, do this with all the instrument which is called a "clepsedre," and it has this form: 
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three holes: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and its tube is made so that the medicine it carries will be such that it well stops up the penis without addition, so that one can draw out moisture and inject when necessary; and when you see your medicines going into the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture and draw with the syringe that is inside; draw the moisture up into the syringe and then push the syringe strongly back in; the moisture will enter inside and come to the bladder now so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: this is it: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of horn, and the head is higher; and below at the breast where the loin joint; then take a bladder of a sheep and put the moisture which you see to enema in the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the pot with that moisture over the fire; then put the head of the enema into the penis, then hold your hand on the bladder with all the moisture coming up, as long as the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don't have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it roundly around; then put the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dish, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and we have said the difference between a stone lodged as rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one must work by incision; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone lodged in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign that sharp pain shoots from the bladder seeming like sharp pain in its subtlety; and it opens the urethra, and grates the patient's penis, and he can urinate many times, and then becomes rigid; and at many of these pains, the urination stops; and healing is easier for children until they are four years old, and is very troublesome for the elderly, and is in the middle for those who are between youth and old age; and it is easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient by enema, to draw out all the phlegm that is in the bowels. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders the search for the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and pull and move them downward so that the stone descends to the opening of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from there; then have him sit between your hands evenly placed, with his hands under his thighs so that the bladder is all sloping downwards; then search for and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut upon the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if you do not feel it at all by touching, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is feverish, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and fully grown; and insert it into his rectum, and search for the stone; and when you feel it with your finger, hold it at the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and guide it out where you see to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend the testicles upwards with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin below the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then he inserts the scalpel cutting, of which this is the form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between what is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; and let it be straight upon the stone, and your two hands should be then at the fundament, and let the incision be traversed so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perchance press so the hand which is at the fundament, that it leaps forth without labor; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: if these are grated they are easier to remove; and if there are some which are underneath, similar to a hazelnut, and round, their removal is easier. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	Wherefore then if it has angles and a margin, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you should pull it up with forceps which are also like a file at the head, to pull out the stone so that it does not escape; or you put underneath a subtle instrument bent at the head; and if you cannot fit it in this way, enlarge the puncture, the opening, and if the stone is sharp, remove it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, then put the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then cut up above, then pull it out hard, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be sewn and a larger incision made. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out immediately because the veins cannot be sutured; but nevertheless, you should strive to draw it out, or break it up with forceps, as much as you can draw it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, and remove it, and put a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water on top to soothe the hot abscess; then let the patient rest on his back, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if it rises very well from the place of oil and water, then cure it with ointment diaphanicon and ointment basilic, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this, urine which is known in a certain way so that without straining with the urine: put then your finger into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and rot it; then lift the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help it in all the ways that you know, until it is healed; and it must be that every hour when you cure it, that you bind both thighs together, and assemble the medicines upon the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it is or leads from the penis and lodges in, and urine cannot pass; so cure this as I have said before, that you cut it many times, and an excuse for the cutting by this cure.  
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have seen this happen myself. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron fork according to this shape and let it have three prongs fixed in the fire: 
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the fork into the shaft gently until it reaches the stone; and turn the fork in your hand within the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone through to the other side; urine will soon come forth, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is quickly broken and comes out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this because something prevents it, then tie a thread below the stone and the other above, then cut into the shaft near the stone between the two threads, then extract it forcefully, untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It sometimes happens that a stone is lodged in women, and if this ever occurs, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to uncover herself to her mirror, especially when she is chaste.  
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman who knows well this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of a woman is deeper lodged than the stone of a man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if these necessities arise, it is fitting that you take a midwife who knows well, and at pains one finds her, and if you do not find her, no less a chaste mirror subtle; and present her with a good wise woman in the life of women or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquest of the stone; and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: then she must put her finger or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it below her finger, and recommend that she put her finger in the malaide, and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder formant. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then press upon the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, where it is moved and felt, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above the stone or below, and make the incision at first small; then put the knife into the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound as much as the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have points. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the likenesses to know the outcome.  
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood comes, put ground vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of the stone from men to help you in your work; and if the blood comes, and it is from the artery that has been cut, put the powder on the spot and bind it with bandages and cloths, and do not start again with this one, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest the patient die by chance; then treat the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is subsided, and the swelling has decreased, you may return to your work, as long as the stone remains hard. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery hernia is nothing other than an accumulation of moisture or white slime that is beneath the heart of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "slime," and it is sometimes properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white slime that we have mentioned; and this does not have a prick. 
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from weakness which comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread.  
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is yellowish, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it is white slime as we have said, it is a boil of the testis, a long prick as the shape of an egg, and it does not show the testicle, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the very fabric, the abscess reunites with a part of the egg, and therefore one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, it is felt well; then when you see the color of the moisture, test all of the instrument as described before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, which comes after the instrument, judge what is inside. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we heal it with iron, it is fitting that the patient be cleansed according to our power and the repletion of his body; then lay him on his back, on something a foot high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left, and command the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the penis towards one of the two ribs of the scrotum; then take the scalpel sharp, and cut the skin of the scrotum along its length up to the groin, and let your incision be straight by dividing the skin of the scrotum up to the white membrane, and flay it subtly according to our power; then pierce the membrane full of fluid with a large hole, and draw out all the fluid, and then put in your ointments, and stretch the membrane upwards; and do not touch the heart of the testicles, but only the membrane; cut all or piece by piece subtly the side of it, for if you do not cut it wisely, the fluid will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, replace it in its place when you have finished the work on the membrane; then unite the two edges of the heart of the testicles with a suture, and then heal it as other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspensory, doubting the flow of blood; then cut the cord at all the suspensory parts, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the artery is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound linen moistened with rose oil; and put another linen moistened with wine and oil on the two cords, and put doubled cloths on top, and tie it all up according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and fill them with finely shredded linen according to this appearance and have them joined together by stitching at the throat of the breeches, one of the ends takes hold onto the base up to the back, and the other to the handle part; and the other two chiefs on the two angles, and let all the restraint be assembled in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this branch is cauterized instead of being cut with a blade of iron, and it is that you take a subtle culinary cautery, and cut the skin of the cords, and heat it as we have said, so that the white sac containing the artery is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that sac at once, and scald it with this subtle hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup in all the ways that you can, so long as you eradicate everything; and keep the fire from touching the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and be careful of running of blood, and milder than the works of cutting; and if anything opposes you, or an abscess breaks or running of blood or something else, then treat what opposes you according to what has been said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then make a perforation as I tell you, and know that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that rarefied water is there, then let the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess at the bottom part all along the spatulum wide, and place the perforation as long as the body; and make the opening large so that all the pus may run out; then put cotton on the place and bind it and leave it for the remaining pus to run out, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not let the pus come out at the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you put a feather or the instrument with which one treats the pus of dropsy, of which form is before; and enlarge the spot on the wound, and know that the pus returns and gathers after six months or thereabouts, and when it has gathered as before, then the patient will pass his days like this. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the thighs 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the incision of this branch, fear leads to several complications, for which it seems to me that one should leave it; and I will tell you the work and the likenesses of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come on the body, and especially on the thighs; and this is by many means. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by superfluity sour and sharp, which is spread on the thighs, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no pain found, and it is a grieving abscess; and by chance are some abscesses grieved painful and hard, and dark colored, and sometimes comes from a new artery, or swelling of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a new artery, it is known by the disposition of the hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it does not behoove that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of a vein swelling is known by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the cut on this resemblance, and on the other carts; and it is that you cut the heart of the onions, then lift the egg high, and draw the thread through the white part, and deliver the suspensoire from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already soldered with these carts new, then it is necessary that you draw the egg, and cut; and if it is aired in the white part, or in that which is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that tension, and cut roundly. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cart is or place behind, then it is necessary that you cut all of it, and draw out the egg, as we have said. 
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks 
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped in a covering resembling a boil, with the softening of the buttocks, and the patient groans when he walks; and the cure of this disease is as much feared as the one before it, nevertheless we will tell you its treatment, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspensory of the buttocks down to your thighs, on all the vessels which are near the penis, and hold them, and extend them; then cut with a sharp scalpel in two places, exposing the vessels, then flay from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle where it has a double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein came, and tie it directly to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound like the others where you use ointment, so that no vessel bleeds, or nourishes one of the buttocks; for by this means there is no harm, and if all the vessels appear visible, it is necessary to drain the buttocks through all the vessels; so that the penis does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be aided.  
de la routure dou syfac	Of the fracture of the bone. 
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are by the section that comes or goes to the bone, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that fracture to one of the coions; and this fracture is either of the bone, or of the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes: either from percussion, or from a leap, or from a fall, or from lifting something too heavy, and by similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the bone are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal even towards the end, because the bone pushes the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the bone, that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear different, under the skin nearby, and this is because of the exit of the intestines and the body outside the bone. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never disentangle the bowels with the intestine, and it is retained therein, and causes great pain to suffer for the patient, even when it is pressed. 
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron out of fear, for which it is convenient to avoid them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;
