et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is such that you command the patient to knead the intestine with his hand inside the wound, if he can reenter; then it is squeezed on its neck between your hands and lifted the thighs; then extend the heart above, and cut all the skin of the testicles from length; then put into the folds of the waist a needle according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the bones can come out; then flay the fascia that is below the skin of the testicles until the white fascia hard is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger in that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white fascia that is below the skin of the egg, and between the second fascia; and part what is behind the egg, and between the second fascia; and then move with your right hand into the heart of the testicles and extend the white fascia upwards to your left hand, and lift the egg to all the fascia towards the waist; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and loosen what is behind the ligature; and see with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped or white hard fascia, and if you find anything, put it in the belly below; then take a needle where it has a thick thread made of 10 threads, and put it into the back part of the fascia, which is after the skin of the testicles; then cut the ends that appear from the threads until there are 4 threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in a cross shape and tie the fascia, of which we said that it is below the skin of the testicles, with a strong ligature of 2 parts; then wrap the ends of the threads and tie them in a form of 2 parts so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter, and no abscess comes in; and put on top the ligature according to the first ligature long 2 fingers from it, and after these two ligatures leave the fascia which is below the heart of the testicles the size of a finger; and afterwards all the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the testicles until the vein and the artery are severed, as we have said before; then administer wool moistened in oil, and apply it to the wounds, and administer the ligature that we said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never is cauterized the white flesh as we have said, after incision, for fear of stopping the blood. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the ligature as long as it bleeds through it; and if it is slow to stop, then apply a dressing of hot water, and put on what we have said, until it bleeds; then heal the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron. 
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done as in the branch which is together with the vein, in part the way you tie the vessels, after cutting above lightly below; then cut in half, and heal the abscess of him who works until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture comes in the groin, as we have said, and opens the veins; and no intestines should be drawn out of the joints, and if some are drawn out, it is a small amount, and they rejoin every hour; and however, if it remains too long in this state, the wound or fistula grows, as long as the intestine is drawn out; and this happens by the extension of the fistula which is in the groin, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swells the veins and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this way: and that is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cauterize the place of the rupture swollen to a width according to the quantity of three fingers; and then draw out the fistula which is under the skin from habit, then take the hot iron and put it on the place appearing of the fistula; and press it down firmly against the belly, then cut the two veins appearing of the fistula on the top of the iron, and cut one and the other; then draw out the top of the iron, and do not cauterize the fistula nor stretch the one or the other, as I have told you in the cure of the rupture of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, let him dress and heal the wound until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is constrained and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is milder in this place and closer to healing. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles 
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the cords that are inside are softened, and it is made to be seen; and it is necessary, when one wishes to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts the softened skin above the natural skin; then brings together the two lips with a suture, and if you see fit, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin in three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and treat it as other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread. 
dou chastrement	punishment 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that punishment is begun in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; but it is necessary only for two ways: one of which is that the sick person can answer when asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we often have need of the punishment of certain beasts to help us, such as a goat and a sheep and a dog and other beasts. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that punishments are done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water, as long as the bowels are softened and hang down; then take them with your hand, as long as they are placed back and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of a beast: it is fitting that you hold the beast and press its skin at its testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut on each eye with one cut when you have well flayed them; and leave no blemish or delicate blemish which is on the vessels; and this manner of castration is better than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction some things of the testicles may remain by chance, by which the beast desires lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodism is according to two manners as men: one so that between the two testicles it appears also as the shape of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes even urinates in the manner. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has upon the vulva also as a penis and two testicles. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is such that you cut away all the added flesh, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, men whose urine leaks through the skin of their testicles, there is no cure. 
de la tentigene	of the tentativeness
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tentigene is added flesh upon the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is fitting that you hold the excess of the tentigene in your hand or at your forceps, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep so that blood does not flow forth, then treat it with other cures until it is healed; and for another flesh that grows at the mouth of the womb, and swells, and perhaps bursts, and looks like a cow's udder, and because of this the ancients called it "cow udder disease." 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you treat it as we have said to the tendon, and the treatment until it is healed. 
de erratique	of a wanderer
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is called erratique when the nature of woman is not perceived, or the parts are small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by illness that has come; or by chariot added, or subtle stuff or hope, and it is made perfect in the marrow, or in the ribs, or underneath, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers; and the knowledge of these is by looking at the belly. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppages are close together, so that they are two or three to the right. 
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is of subtle stuff, and they are close to the two leaves, then hurry and do this: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the two leaves, so that the subtle stuff is gone, and the stoppages are removed; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and let the woman sleep with a man each day so that she cannot be without. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the bone marrow is hard and thick, it is fitting that you cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is from a chariot wheel, suspend it with an awl and cut it; and have medicines to staunch the blood, such as alum, dragon's blood, frankincense, mixed abundantly with egg white; then apply a cane of lead wide enough so that the wound cannot close; and thus leave it for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then let it be treated by other remedies until it is healed.  
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a chariot wheel comes to the marrow, it is fitting to cut it according to this manner, except if it is an inflamed abscess. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For a festering abscess that is in the marrow, one should not touch it with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which do not usually bleed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; and as we have said in the chapter the resemblances of others, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and hardness, when they are perfected in the anus, and they do not appear to the touch, unless it is cured by iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the anus, one can feel, are those which one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore it is fitting that you put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the hardness with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle powders on medicines that restrain blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and gallnuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it goes out, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have cupping glasses applied to his back and breasts without pricking; then take flax, moisten it in plantain juice or ivy juice with old wine, and apply it to the area. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a hard head, so you must cover it as I have said for the thelul; and then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow  
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the marrow, such as sores and putrid abscesses and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I say in this treatise about the hot abscess which comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses which collect pus; and if you wish to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.  
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it ripen until the pain is relieved; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he can lean, and support himself on his back and assemble his feet at the parts further from the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then turn him toward the right side, and he will administer the instrument which works the mouth of the marrow, the form of which will come later; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument administered, you insert the point first to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary for him to put the funnel of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and one presses it gently with the hand, if it is necessary to cover the head, put a bandage on the wound; and when the bowels are emptied, you must put into the wound tents softened in rose oil or green oil; and place the tent firmly from the wound to the margin of the skin, and put over the skin and on the poultice clean linen softened in water where chives or leeks have been cooked; then treat afterwards for two days with ointment suitable for this, until it is healed; and never raise the skin and the wound by an enema of water and honey, and then of water with long-cooked roots of lily and aristoloche; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is rejoined at the skin margin, you must be careful not to cauterize it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth 
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if it is when you see the woman hurry down, and desire to smell the air: then the child will hasten to come out; then you know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and that the issue is under her head, and the secondine with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press her belly lightly so that the child comes out quickly; for when he descends on his head, the secondine follows with him, and the woman is delivered from her superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes on its feet, and the body or shoulders come out first, or the hands, or it comes on its belly, or backwards, and is converted by chance through its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help her. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its own head through natural birth and the woman gives birth grievously and her strength is weak, let her sit on a saddle which women hold; and make rise her nature with oil or fenugreek that is cooked, then insert the small spatula between her thighs, of which this is the shape: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the secondine and press at her finger until the moisture that is within runs out; and take hold of the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman an enema of fenugreek broth with sesame oil; then let her drink and sneeze from mustard, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then now she will deliver the child. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out further, then it is necessary that you gently reset them bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a stool, and raise her feet upward; then overturn the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when overturned; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cut the hands with the knife which is mentioned before, and extract the child, and reset it evenly. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the delivery of a child onto its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, if it is crooked, straighten it up; and then turn it bit by bit until it is straight; then take it by the feet and extend it bit by bit. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to its thighs, if commanded to grasp, and make it sneeze from constraint; if it jumps far, God willing. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not strong as we have said, then turn it bit by bit until it conforms to the natural form. 
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be light. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come strong as we have said, take muscilage of hollyhock, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and anoint with this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, make her a collar of myrrh, and put it below, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and pull out her mouth and nose, and take hold of her belly lightly, for the child will now jump. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child upon its knees 
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if it puts its hands on its belly little by little; then let it be swaddled upon its neck, and let its feet hang down, and let it lie outside of the bed; and fold its hands little by little, and then take its hands onto the belly, and remove the cushions from underneath, as long as it is brought low; and if the child does not jump, then take its feet and move them upwards, then move the belly up, and then push with your hands; and lift the child little by little; and instruct the woman to hold on while the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child who comes forth with one hand hanging down 
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	it is necessary to endeavor to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, let the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, let her lie on the bed and straighten her legs; then administer the muscilage which I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, let her sit on a stool, and then study to bring back the hand; and lift the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold on while the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child upon its neck and has spread its hands and its face turned towards its mother's back 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is fitting that the midwife holds her hand, then turns it little by little, and lifts it lightly; and when it is equalized, she puts on the natural musky mixture of honey and oil, as we have said, then commands her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a stool, and command her to grasp; and make her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the afterbirth 
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes forcefully in this manner for all the afterbirth, grasp the afterbirth at your fingernail, as long as the moisture is emptied; and if the infant can lie upon its face and upon its neck, grasp it from the shoulder, so that it is not retained, and the infant dies; then push the infant inside, as long as you have put it as it should be, and command the woman to grasp herself several times: then pull lightly. 
de l’issue des gemelz	from the removal of twins 
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and rarely three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	If they are strange, and do not live, it is seldom named; I know that if they are multiplied, they are separated by the placenta which divides them, which is tied to the belly button; and sometimes they also issue naturally as one under all others, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born crooked, the cure is as we have said, and let the midwife be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does; and do so as it is worth bringing to safety.  
de plusors enfans	of multiple children 
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is fitting that the midwife knows all this, for adventure similar things happen; if she does according to what is fitting. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman who has lost her child or is pregnant and there is no expulsion, and you are forced to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound constitution and does not have any other ailment or fear of death. It is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, with her hips inclined downward, and her legs raised. The minister holds the woman's two thighs so she is tied to the bed so that she is not shaken during the delivery of the child. Then rub the mouth of the midwife with moist oils mixed with marshmallow and fenugreek and flaxseed; then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and mixtures. Then gently insert her fingers into the midwife's vagina, taking care to place them in suitable places; take care that if the child is seen to descend upon its head, insert the fingers into her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the throat or near the ribs. And if the descent is on its feet, insert it at the knees and midriff; and it is necessary that he hold the finger in his right hand, and place the curve between his two fingers of his left hand, and gently insert it with his whole hand into any of these places that we have mentioned until he reaches the empty space. And this is the form of the finger:  
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place it against the other forceps, or the third if you need them, so that the extraction is equal; and then extend them equally by moving from one side to the other, to make it come out, and let the forceps have teeth to hold it, as this is its shape: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, anoint the wound with some of its two points of oil, and insert them into that part, and draw out the other part; and if none remains, put these forceps or higher up, and do this until it all comes out. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back due to tightness, then you must wrap it up in a cloth until it is all out; then hold it at the joint of the palm or at the wrist, and thus you should do the same with the other hand, and the two feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or if it has a sharp point assembled, then you should insert the pointed spatula between your fingers, and cut the head and extract the point; or you can cut it with an instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with instruments or chapters that follow this one; and in the same way do so if the infant has a naturally large head; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head jumps out and is extracted with force, split it as much as the moisture that is in its lower part comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as small as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you should pierce it so that the moisture runs. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infant is on its feet, the attraction is slight, and the drawing towards the mouth of the womb is slight. 
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is embedded in the belly or breast, it is fitting that you extract it wrapped in a cloth held on the hand; and pressing the belly or breast, until the moisture which is there runs out; and if the other limbs are removed, and the head remains, then put your hand upon it perfumed with marjoram, and draw it up to the mouth of the marris; then put one or two ounces, and pull hard; and if the mouth of the marris is constricted by a hot boil which has come there, it is not fitting to work on it, but rather to administer moist and fatty things; and apply poultices, and make them soft and moistening. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, then apply what we have said in the living child; and if there is no power, then pull it out piece by piece, and leave nothing of the afterbirth. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it minister what we said in abscesses which come in the marsh; and if bleeding comes, let it be put in sharp restraint, and minister other remedies. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had been dead, then conceived another upon that one, and brought forth the others dead. 
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time an abscess came to her buttock, and it swelled so much that it burst open, and she began to have a great discharge. 
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, for the belly has no bones. 
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought they were the bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I searched the wound and found bones, as long as the woman was in better condition; and I left the woman for a long time like that, and there remained only a little bit of bone at its place; and I have not recounted this chapter except for the fact that when masters find a strange thing they know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the marrow to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the shape of the pressor, with which we squeeze the books; and at two turns are two heads of two ligatures. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than those of the restrictor and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood I should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the trees should be one finger, and a palm and a half long; and between the two ligatures there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which should be fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are put in the mouth of the marrow to open when you turn the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, of its likeness more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony wood or boxwood, according to the likeness of tongs; and it has two jaws with two adjustments, as you see, a palm long and two fingers wide; and when you see the vulva open for the whole instrument, make the woman sit on her bed, the feet hanging and the legs open, then push the two adjustments together into the vulva and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand along the whole instrument, as you have done with tongs equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vulva, so long as the woman does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all assembled and their resemblances are multiplied; and when the women have them aligned, the work is so much faster, and higher are men for their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despair of the instrument until you have prepared it, for its necessity is inexcusable. 
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, it is fitting that you instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then cause her to sneeze forcefully, and remove your hands from her mouth and nose; and if she does so, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not work, take a pot and make a hole or cover in it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over the fire; then place one end of a cane or tube into the pot and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and hold it there until the vapors enter the womb; then cause her to sneeze as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second bone jumps hastily. 
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not strong, command the healer to moisten their left hand in sesame oil or hollyhock mucilage, and then put it into the wound, and seek the second bone; and when they have found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straight so that the marrow does not break during extraction; but one must move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come and loosen. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the marrow is narrow and constricted, we have said the cure is sneezing, and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, be careful not to pull; but it is necessary that he who is at the opening of the marrow, tie it to the thigh of a woman, then give an enema of tetrapharmacon ointment; it will carry it away and put it back in place, and it will become strong. But nevertheless, when it carries it away there comes a bad odor to the stomach and head, and weakens the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is fitting then to use appropriate fumigations for this: none of the ancients have tried a fumigation of watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for retention of flowers and the secundines is this: 
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is shaped like a cane, and one puts the thin end in the opening, and the wide sides over the fire; and let the fumigations be on the coals, until the smoke is gone, and then begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation 
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but rather it is blocked by a thin membrane: so it behooves the midwife to pierce that membrane with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp knife, and keep the pressure so she does not touch it; then place a cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will remain in place, put or insert a cane of wood, and leave it for three days, and have it removed when the child wants to go to the nursery. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And it sometimes happens that this dislocation comes from the healing of a wound or an abscess; so you must cover that healing: if it is cured, as we have said about the cane of wood. 
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the bottom
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the fundament are swellings and thickenings that come from behind the fundament or in the space between the two parts; if there is one fistula or several; and when this swelling is old, it works, and still moistures ooze white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and they are known by those who experience discharge or flatulence when the patient makes a bowel movement, and perhaps even jump once.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder and to half of the penis; and they reach as far as the juncture of the thigh, and up to the knee. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes the fistula penetrating at the base, and not penetrating; and it is that you insert your second finger or thumb into the base, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, then insert a tent of fine linen thread or horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and nothing exits in terms of discharge, flatulence, or worms as we have said: know that it does not pierce through; then hasten to cleanse it. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates as far as the bladder or the urethral canal, then the urine leaks out and cannot be retained by medicine. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced as far as the joint of the thigh, so the tent comes to the place; if there is no crookedness and the location of the pain is around, then it will be better soon, and no medicine nor ointment is of any use; and in these fistulas that are passing, there is no cure except toil, and vanity of foolish remedies which interfere. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not passing and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced; and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a tent of iron, or of lead if there is crookedness, as far as you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the foundation, it is fitting that you put your two index fingers in, and if you then feel that the tent has pierced it; and be uncovered where you feel between your finger the sinew or the flesh, then you know that it is passing; if there is no working, one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We say that one can heal some well, but this happens rarely; and the help one does, if it heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula as it is said before; and puts it all hot into the fistula until it reaches the bottom; and do this two or three times, until you know that these bad humors are burnt, which resemble a bird's feather; then cure with bandages softened in butter, until those humors dry out, then cure with ointment joining flesh and soldering.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters, and does not reach the bottom which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or sinew between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula under this covering from the heart; then cut off the beginning of the fistula, and put it forward before the tent, and apply the cautery afterward until it reaches the head of the tent; and the tent will be delivered and fall away; then cleanse those bad humors that resemble a bird's feather, so that none remain. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if pain comes, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For cauterization with fire brings two good things: that is to say, the burning of these charred herbs, and the stemming of blood and drying of moisture; then the treatment of softened tents in butter or crushed hazelnuts, as long as the wounds swell up, and if the flesh burns in the swelling; then treat the wound with ointments made from strong, hard herbs. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the fundament and is distant from the body, put it back in its place with a probe or foundation, and inquire about it.  
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and between it are two layers of cloth or linen or herbs, where it is about to perforate, then there is no other way but a path of trust and hope through the administration of one of three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it down to its base, or if you can put tents in and treat them as before; and do not go too deep, lest you cut the ligament that holds the fundament, and voluntary discharges come through the wound; then treat it as we have said. Perhaps it will be healed, or remove the covering and cleanse it after it is cut away from the fundament, either by a tent or another pointed instrument; then cleanse the faulty flesh that is in the wound as much as you can; then try to restore the wound and keep the fistula in the part behind the fundament: this would be easier for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side near the base under the skin above, then take a pierced tent at its head according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put the twisted thread in two, and put the tent on all the thread into the fistula until it is at its head. 
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin near the base inside, then draw out the thread from that hole, so that you put your finger or the base; and take hold of the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and pull one against the other, and leave it for one or two days; and restrain it sometimes, until the threads catch those scars which are between them, and tighten; then treat the wound until it is closed and healed.  
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too tight. 
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make a bandage too tight, then apply a remedy as we have said, until it is healed. 
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spathicula used to make a fistula must be very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, because you should not cut what you ought not to cut as you see here: 
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often bleed, and there may be one or several, and they protrude from the fundament and at its head; but those which protrude have little moisture, and sometimes bleed a little or secrete a little yellow fluid, and they have the color of flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the fundament is that you order the patient to strain to go to the bathroom, as long as the fundament relaxes and the threads appear; if he hesitates, and it can be grasped with tweezers, or held by your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if the thread cannot be held because of moisture, grasp them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them off, and sprinkle some hot powders that are in place of a cautery on top; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure them with other remedies until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot relax, give the patient an enema of a sharp and sour purgative to cleanse what is in the fundament so that it can come out openly; when the patient strains, and the threads are loose from the fundament, the cure is easy; and it is that you grasp them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them off, then cure them as we have said until they are healed, and he fears incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is fitting that you administer the suture according to this manner: take a twisted thread and put it into a needle, then draw the thread above and make the needle pierce through the other side, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and if it be wide; and remove the formed thread, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all others, and leave one to correct the excess blood; then put on the foundation a softened cloth moistened in rose oil or cerate, and put on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let it be until they fall out, and when they have fallen out, cure them with ointment and other cures, until it is healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	on the drying of the wounds or foundation  
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying of wounds in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no avail. 
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary, you should scrape off the bark with the point of a knife or your fingernail, so that it does not become moist; then treat it until it is healed as it should be; and if it cannot heal, begin the scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well and is scraped, then treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	You tremble. 
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small false appearance under the skin, and it goes very far apart; and one never finds it cold, and one also feels it as if dead with trembling, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that cane on top of the trembling, so that the circles completely surround the trembling; then turn your hand around the whole cane until you grasp all around the trembling, and put it very far, and uproot the trembling from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a chain of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle underneath and draw above: 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, for it must hold onto the pain, and press. And if you see, do this cauterization of the tremor, as it is before or chapter of the cautery. 
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a clyster 
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or artichoke, or of melted iron or malleable; and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then that are administered in the care of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.  
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster, small and large, is wide above, where the belly is tied according to this manner:  
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a severance where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced within; and it has on one side two holes, and on the other one; and the belly is where one puts the medicines from a bladder of an animal or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there is a space of one finger between each hole, then put into these holes a strong thread of raw silk twisted in X or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then administer an enema; and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then insert it gently; then hold the syringe in both hands together until all is filled, then extract the enema, and have the patient raise his legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it flow as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is of greater help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply a clyster for a disease of intestinal blockage, and the medicine hastens to pass, then repeat it until it is cured. 
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if hemorrhoids are at the base or an abscess, then let the clyster be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of a subtle clyster on which the skin should be drawn out: 
des plaies	of wounds  
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places or parts where the wounds are made, and by what they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by a blow of a stone, and a cut of a sword or knife, or lance, or club, or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or foot, or belly, or liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for remembrance will come in its chapter.  
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if you are careful it is from a blow of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt a hot abscess: then make it heal quickly from the cephalic vein itself if there is little blood from the wound, and let the healing be on the contrary side of the injured part; and forbid the patient to eat wine and rich meats.
