Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to heal, let his food be reduced and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if a hot abscess should come, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if he who has it has moved it, put some ointments on it until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a swordsman's cut and similar ones, and the edges cannot be brought together by stitching, then assemble them with sutures as I will say for abdominal wounds and their suturing. 
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and it can be grasped but only by a single point, then cauterize it; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat large meats such as beef and boiled wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotting flesh and it does not reach the bone, then cauterize all the rot thoroughly and deeply, and treat it afterward; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound which, without cutting, cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie off the artery; and if you find it dislocated, tie it with thread; and if this does not work, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: and it is that you put this powder on it which will bind it together so as the fire has melted it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and powder it subtly, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, as long as it heats well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this with quicklime alone, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has melted the wound. 
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has melted the wound, immediately in this way, one does not put this powder on it; but puts some digested ointments or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it flows freely; then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you here after about the fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the neck 
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut. 
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to let the wound heal and apply nothing constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain which is the highest member; but let the medicine be below, such as chamomile washed in clear water, and mixed with rose oil, and also comfrey washed in clear water, and other mineral stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.  
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed. 
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is raised and full of pus, pierce it lower; and if the artery is cut, and a flow of blood comes forth, bind it, tie it off, and cauterize it as needed; and if the spine in the throat is cut, or the heart, and the passage is kept closed so that the meat goes through, sew the heart onto the neck bone and do not touch the throat but put it back together according to its natural shape; then remove it carefully and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, carve it; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them out with tongs as much as you can, and those that you cannot get, leave them until the wound rots, becomes detached, and its path is clear; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on the powder I have mentioned. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in this chapter. 
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a spear or knife wound 
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if there is wind coming from the wound while the patient breathes: then know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in it for the first hour, nor bind it because the blood will not flow freely, return to the heart, and kill the patient; but apply an attractive ointment and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have an ointment, place old cotton in the wound to draw out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days or four or more; if there is no spasm, trembling, evil heart, or strangeness of breath; then when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.  
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal then with tents and other cures, as long as it heals; and if it cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; if the cure is as one should. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, whether on the front, back, or side; if the cure of that which is in front; if it is large, by suture; and if it is small, by powder; and if it penetrates the bone, and has broken pieces, then wash the wound, and treat the fractures if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound rot so that the extractions are easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of rupture of the belly 
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Ruptures of the belly are large, medium, and small; from a large wound sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude, allowing entry for others; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because it is more difficult to put the intestines back in unless they are returned one by one, because the intestine swells quickly when it feels cold and does not go back in easily. Therefore, a medium-sized wound is preferable because one can return the intestine to its place as with others. And know that rupture of the belly occurs according to four manners: the two common sutures occur at the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and the other two proper sutures are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are cleaner with the suture of the belly, and I will say one by one and explain. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines is protruding, and there is little to put back in place, it can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in two ways: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or you cook in lukewarm water squinant and cypress and spikenard, and lift the intestines as long as the swelling is removed; and never do this with restraining bandages, but loosen them so that there is only gentle pressure to reduce swelling. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with lukewarm water or broth if they are cooked, for this widens the entrance to receive things; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used for hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is looser than the size of the wound so that we should not cut except in great necessity; and these are the instruments for splitting: if you cut inside the curve and do not go beyond, and see this shape: 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, if you can put them back into their natural form in their proper place, do so, for this is worth much. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, it is fitting that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your understanding into this so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is fitting to administer what I say in large and small wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds put what seems fitting to you, then have in your hands a minister who holds the entire rupture with his hand, and brings together the lips; and this is the common way of sutures, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a space of two fingers, and put in a needle where there is a good strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the sinew, which is below the skin within, as far as you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two edges of the sinew together four-fold; then draw it tight with a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two edges of the wound evenly, and then leave a space of two fingers, and put in another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need needles, as long as the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, for thin needles pierce all the flesh, and those too thick cannot enter well: therefore it is fitting that they are medium-sized; and it is not fitting to push the needles too far from the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths at the ends of the needles for them to hold, and leave them as long as the wound is healed; and this way of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for in it one uses a needle or two.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I put the intestines back in place after they had been out for 24 hours and the wound was sutured for 15 days and I treated it and he was healed.  
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And those who saw him thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water and honey until he was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and pass it from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced through straight, take the head of the thread or twine or whatever you have passed the needle through and make it pierce through on the other side from the inner part to the outer; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the furriers do with furs, and that you leave one time the thread on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the whole suture is completed. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suturing, which Galen properly calls, is this as some do, who bring together the two parts naturally, and apply one end of the thread to the other end, in this way: put a needle or the end of a thread close by, and pierce that place only, and leave the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle and pierce it from the further part until it is inside, with the two ends of the thread; then pierce one and the other from the further part until it is inside, in two other ends of the thread which are on the other side; and this is the gentler manner of suturing and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and some testify to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one must put one needle in on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than in other places of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of a wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as if the fire has moved it, so replace the intestine and the suture; then put on powder containing charcoal, and if the fire has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound swells; and sew the thread, and let the siphons and the mirach be soldered; then treat the wound as other wounds until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to swell, old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicine in several positions unless the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause contagion to the main members, it is fitting that you moisten linen lightly in tempered oil, or in rose oil, and put it around the groin, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then give enemas of warm red wine, and similarly if the putrefaction comes up to the intestines; and pierce within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the fineness of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity to the nature of the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the gut protrudes from the wound, put it back as you would the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must bind the place which is black so that blood does not flow into it, because there are veins and arteries there; then cut away what is between the ligatures, and hang the two ends down from the part below the wound until it comes out to ease the extraction when the gut bursts, and the wound opens. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, then it can be restored in some men, for I have seen a man who was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it festered and became a fistula, and there was discharge from it and flatulence; I treated it according to what I could, and did not stop trying to heal it until it was healed, and the edges were joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it soldered, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he did not have any pain, but remained in better condition, and ate and drank; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be tied in this way: take tweezers with large heads, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the tweezers have opened the mouth, place them on the two lips so that they tighten their mouths; and then cut off the head, and this remains so that it cannot loosen, then put another tweezer afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is all closed up; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These heads burn in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the head of this intestinal thread that has been well stripped, and then tie to the head of this thread a fine linen thread twisted together, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and reset it in the rupture; and this manner of stitching with tweezers is nothing more than according to the way of skill and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no remedy or healing except subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be 
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes old, is universally called "fistula," and even when it is healed and goes inward. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its greenness, a hard and white nodule, where no pain is felt, and it is also raised like the feather of a bird; sometimes it has a clear opening inward, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times large enough. And I have spoken of it in the division of wounds that any wound that is not healed and there is no flesh, it is due to one of the nine causes: namely, by the thinness of blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, which does not allow flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or because the wound is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or because the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the nature of the region is slow to digest and heal, and swells by nature; or because there are veins or bones. And I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and their cures with medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary that I make you know the treatment of fistula which is made by handwork. 
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if it happens to come to the principle quality of the primary member, and similar things. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are grievous to heal, and there is nothing else except labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come up to the place I have said, and you are confident in its cure and you see it known, take a probe of iron or brass, if the fistula is straight; and if it is crooked, use a subtle probe of lead, for lead bends easily around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it by probes, cauterize it through one of the openings, for moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then lance it freely according to your ability, so that you know whether there are bones or nerves, and it is cleansed perfectly, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut it according to what I have told you, and remove the corrupt matter and the decayed flesh that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, it is necessary that you cut deeply as much as you can, then put softened probes soaked in medicinal water into it, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments promoting healthy flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it away.  
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If veins or nerves do not hinder you or the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, dig out all the corruption until it is entirely removed, then treat the matter with healing remedies until it is healed; and if it is not healed and returns to its former state, know that you have not gone far enough: dig deeper and clear as much as you can until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with forceps, extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, treat them all the same way, and do not leave any; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut through the moisture and flesh and free the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something promoting rot on the wound, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will be removed more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, let the corruption only continue until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part that is corrupted and comes to the marrow of the bone, then you must sew and cover everything up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is joined; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and it swelled into a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but those who looked after him foolishly worked so much on it that they opened the abscess, and they corrupted much of the matter, and it became a fistula, and there were many openings from which they all flowed with pus and moisture from the body; and many healers treated him for two years, and he had no success in the art of hands until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and those who corrupted it through the openings into a large body; and the flesh of the young man became red, and had a citrine color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I hammered a tent into one of these holes, and then I examined all the holes, and found that some came against each other from all sides of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and probed into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came to the bone inside; I cut away what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and I began to restore the wound with medicines for a long time, and could not solder it; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and cut it away, and tried to solder the place; but I could not until I probed around a palm of the bone, and cut away all its marrow, then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and soldered quickly, and did not need to be started again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation often bled, but he was healed completely and in place of the bone a hard flesh was born, and was of good disposition and had neither harm nor anything contrary at all, neither going nor coming. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be treated in this manner: take a linen cloth and bind it to the head of the bone that appears, and command someone to extend it upwards; and put another woolen cloth larger than the first cloth, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone, and stretch the head so that you draw down the corrupted flesh, and uncover the flesh in the place where you see that it must be treated so that the silk does not stain the flesh; and put a coal or a plank under the bone to help burn the corrupted flesh; and it must be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and treat again another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then put a hot coal underneath, and then from one part to the other burn the corruption, and let the burning be as long as the corruption is deep, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and burn the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut it through; and if the corruption is at the wrist of the hand or at the wrist of the foot, then it is a very serious thing, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not prevent you from doing so; and know that the incisors and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the placement of the bones and the appearance of them, their thickness and their subtlety, their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each semblance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the instrument that you need accordingly. 
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The flesh rots either from within or from without; and when you have medicine that corrodes through the treatment of medicines, and it does not profit, it is necessary to cut off that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from death, or from malice, which is greater, from the lack of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and swells after the blackness, then goes that corrosion from member to member, and takes hold of the whole body; if you hurry in cutting off, and if it is from the sting of some venomous creatures, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the toe, cut it off, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.  
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, cut it off at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut it off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and do the same thing when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut it off after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut off the whole foot; and if it rises to the leg, cut it off at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy except to leave the patient to death; and the manner of cutting off or sewing up the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister's bandage below, and another minister's bandage above, and you sever the flesh that is between the two bandages at a span wide, so that the bone is uncovered; then cut it off or sew it up, and put on each side a cloth of linen, so that the sewing does not touch the healthy place, and brings the patient other injury and abscess.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first came on the back of his foot, so that it spread throughout his entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cut off his foot, and it was healed; and long afterwards the corrosion returned to the back of his hand, and he came to me, and I put repelling things on him after cleansing his body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, because the man's strength was weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and it was healed; and I do not tell this story except so that others may do the same, if they need to. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in fleshy places and stays so long that it gathers a large amount of pus; and then it bursts and discharges, and the pus runs out, and the wound remains open like a vessel; and the skin which is above is as thin as linen cloth, and does not go down to the bone nor to the nerve, and such a sickness is called "healthy," and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin if you cut it all around, even when it is thin like linen cloth; and it does not open because of its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are sure that the skin will burn, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick like flesh, then cure it with an enema thus: see if the breast is large, and the pus which is in it has a foul odor, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take alum, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them into a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need and mix it with water and honey, and give it as an enema into the breast, drawing out the pus; and leave the medicine in for two hours, and then remove it while squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the odor is removed; and never give an enema of water from ash when this medicine is not present, but take ashes from vine wood and pour water over them, then strain it and give it as an enema until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water from ash, then give an enema of water and honey in which there is a pinch of powdered litharge; or give an enema of honey and mead wine which has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the breast breathe; and when you have done this and are sure that the breast is well cleansed, then give an enema of something that produces flesh in it, and take a diachylon plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine; or give an enema of some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken of their properties or have treated them in the book on ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small and the tube of the enema cannot enter, enlarge it a bit with an iron instrument and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, sew it and leave only one place where the enema can enter, and if the opening which discharges pus is above, cut it or a lower place than it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, do not allow char to enter it; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, arrange it in such a way that the bowel runs to the lowest place where it is. For when the bowel is perfect, do not allow char to enter and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, arrange it in this manner: so that the bowel runs lightly down, and leave nothing of the bowel; and take consolidating medicines to put on the healthy part, and spread them on a linen cloth that covers all the healthy part; then cover the strongest place around the perforation of the breast so that it is larger than the first one, then spread ointment frequently on the other cloth according to the quantity of the perforation, and put it on the perforation of the breast to align the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and the one that is on the perforation of the breast, remove often to remove the bowel, and know what runs from the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or enough, whether digested or undigested; and take care whether the patient feels pain or none, and if there is an abscess or not; and when your medicine has been spread in this manner and you see the nature that leaps on the perforation of the breast, know that the breasts are already healing, and approaching health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day; and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast feels bloated and undigested after many days, know that the breast is not healing. 
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons linger for a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men in whom the healing of the wounds lingers, and others who heal quickly; and if the breast remains swollen and undigested after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast is slow to heal and becomes hardened, apply drying medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diachylon ointment, for it contains a large part of vitriol and is the last medicine. Take diachylon ointment and make it with rose oil, and rosewater equal in quantity; then cook it and use it; and when diachylon ointment is not present, take myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on honey when it is taken off the fire; then spread it on linen and apply it to the breast. And sometimes administer long aristolochia and roots of celestial lily, which are also like flour of vetches and centaury; and use them either simple or compound: grind them and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger 
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A boil is an abscess that arises under the fingernail of the hand or foot, or by chance it arises on other toes; and when it is envied, and no heed is paid to it, then it comes a large abscess, and runs and discharges pus as much as it runs to the root of the finger, and by chance runs all the way; and corrosion comes up to the bone, so that there is foul-smelling pain, and the flesh of the toe is swollen, and the color is dark. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluity that remains from the fingernail, then cauterize the wound afterward.  
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses the flesh, and begins to grow in, and the wound, then it is necessary that you put a wedge under the nail so as not to prick the flesh, and push it up, and cut away this flesh subtly and lightly, and apply on the remaining flesh medicinal burning and corrosive agents to remove all; then treat with ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut and treat it deeply, for as long as the corrupted bone is there, it cannot heal; and if you see the corruption spreading, cut into it in one of the ways previously mentioned, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is hard, swollen, and the patient feels great pain, you must first heal it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula, cutting across above it, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on it that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the deafness of the hand 
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The boils that are born on the hands of some men are sometimes all fleshy, and sometimes there is a part where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none others are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some parts of the fingers. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born in any new part of the body do not move, and those who are born at the joint of a bone may move; the size of that which is fleshy so is light, in this manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure; if you hold them, cut them off. 
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For that which is born on the bone or in any new part, it is fitting that you first cut the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone at a suitable size for that, then cure it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come at the bones together come by birth, or by swelling of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things. 
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is fitting that you cut that swelling so that the bones repair according to their natural forms; then put between two bandages or cloths softened in rose oil, so that they do not swell together; or you put between two pieces of fine lead, as long as the flesh is joined together, as it should be. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a wound comes to any of his limbs with the palm, then treat that wound as it should be treated. 
des vils	some old ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large swollen vessels full of melancholic superfluities which come in many parts of the body; and they occur more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer to him sometimes purging with colocynth, and then the herb basil.  
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two manners: one is that you cauterize them and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you tie off the vein and cauterize it all.  
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Bloodletting is done in this manner: First raise the leg with very hot water so that the thick blood becomes thin, then strain the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut a vein in one, two or three places, making a wide incision. Then draw and let out the black blood with your hand, from one side to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can bear; then tie it off and instruct him to abstain from meat containing black cole; and begin again the evacuation and the healing when the veins are full, and harm the patient.  
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the limb is according to this manner: take the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs, then put it in a bath, and apply hot water to the leg until it becomes red, and swells the veins; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and then apply to the place near the long bone at the top of the knee, or in the lower part below the ankle; then cut the skin with a knife and flay the vein from each side, until it appears when touched; and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems as a white rope; then push the arrow under it, until it is raised out of the skin, and then apply it to the knife lightly, and then apply it in another place above it three times; then flay the skin on the vein until it appears, and lift it with the arrow, just as you did, and apply it to another knife, just as you did first; then apply another incision, or more if needed, and lift it, and apply it to the bone of the foot, and pull and lift until the second incision; then extract it from incision to incision, until it comes out entirely, and then apply it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, push a needle through all its strong thread double, tie it, and pull it, and push it under the arrow, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not break, because if it breaks, you can neither pull nor lift it, and it will cause harm to the patient; and when you have treated it all, put wool moistened with wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it completely; and treat it as we have previously said. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved and does not cut completely unless it cuts the vein; and it is of a large curve because if it were delicate, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the form: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in warm parts where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes inside the body snakes and worms, embedded between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the flesh changes color, and the vein begins to come out, just like the root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder is open, it is fitting that you wrap around a piece of flax from three and a half to eleven and a half finger-widths, tie a knot, and leave the flax hanging on the leg, and every time it becomes detached, you should wrap it again around the flax and tie a knot; and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root as long as it is all coming out; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and putrefaction or pus, and evil disease; therefore it is fitting that it should be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains but flesh; and sometimes this vein when it is treated is five handbreadths long, or ten, and one man once came to me, whose was ten handbreadths long, and when you cut it, it will spurt one or two finger-widths, and pierce it through to the bottom so that everything comes out; and let the matter which is inside be emptied, and apply medicines that prevent putrefaction every day, then treat the wound as you would an abscess. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein more than twice, and likewise when it opens at the joint of the foot or leg, and there comes much discharge, and from which it leaps again; treat it then as we have said before.
