des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land “beef disease” because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and the man feels it well from limb to limb as long as it is going beneath the skin where it travels, and jumps far; and it arises from the putrefaction of some humors, just as come worms and snakes and lampreys and roundworms or stomach worms; and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body and ascends to the head and comes to the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens often. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and draining, it cannot be removed unless it goes: so it must be that you bind the place above and below with a strong tight tie, then cut upon it and drain it hard, and if the worm is hidden in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs to the eye as we have said: and if you see it coming or near the eye, remove the eyebrow below it and cut upon it, and drain it hard. And it behooves the patient to cleanse the body with dissolving medicines for putrid humors, and to beware of meats that cause decay. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain which comes from windiness. 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain which comes in some members, and then can move from member to member; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and just after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm on her shoulder, faster than anything else, like living silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place and stuck in her shoulder, and then a little while after ran through all her body, until it reached her other arm; then she told me that it was now turning around her body, just as I saw. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner. 
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had felt pain move from one place to another, but I had never seen it as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins, and therefore this constrained wind appeared; and it does not appear in this way in those who are fleshy and have moist bodies and full veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind above and below hastily, and then cauterize on top until this windiness constrained in place is forced out; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then use a remedy from those who expel windiness, such as foul-smelling pills, serpent pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in bodies where they lodge. 
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those which have large points, and small ones, and barbed, and socketed; and those which have two angles, and those which have flanges, and those which have pieces; and those which lodge in any member lodge according to two manners: either in a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the arrowhead is in any part of the limb and the signs of death which I will tell you later appear to you, it behooves you that you abstain from extracting this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many ways; and when these bad signs do not appear to you and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrowhead is lodged and pierces the bone and the dura mater which is above the brain is severed, is when there is darkening and stupor and turning green and redness in it, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it flows without force from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and there oozes moisture white in appearance like pus from the wound, and it also burns like fire. And if these signs appear to you, then abstain from treatment and leave the arrow where it is if it is not embedded. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seizure when it falls or strikes the heart is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the seizure moves just like a pulse, and brings forth black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death follows. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never leaves the body is that without spurting of foam it leaps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and desires cold air. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls in the covering of the buttock, it is below the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls in the stomach, perhaps something of the undigested flesh leaps from the wound.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the gut or stomach, and it does not pass through the intestine, there is no hope for a cure, nor for extracting the arrow. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and the urine flows and starts to leave, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to several positions. 
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you how it happened to me so that you do otherwise. 
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck or lodged near the tear duct in the root of his nose; I tried it and drew it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any harm. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he treated with a game a dart that had fallen into the fat of the eye below the paper below, and the dart was filled, and could only reach its point towards the fire, and it was a dart large as a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the game was healed, and no evil accident befell him. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And he treated a dart from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic dart with ears: I shaved the beards, and I refined as much as I extracted it, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And he treated a dart to a man that had fallen on his belly, and I thought he would die; and then after he had passed XXX days, it did not change his disposition; I cut above the dart, and I hooked it, and extracted it forcefully, and he did not have any bad accident. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man into whom an arrow has fallen or gone in, and the wound was sutured over it; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural position, nor found any harm in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you see another man into whom an arrow has fallen in his face, and the wound was sutured; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many other similar cases. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow for a prince of the king, which had fallen between his nose, and there was a slight decline to the right side; and the arrow was entirely embedded. I was called upon to treat it after it had fallen for three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.  
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with great subtlety, and did not feel it at all; and he felt numbness and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of an arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the plaster for several days, and stitched up the wound completely, and kept the patient a long time like this, until he felt the arrow one day inside his body; and he told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine sharp and corrosive for several days, until it was opened, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow moving in its place; then I added to the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it healed well within four months, and then I enlarged the wound so that I could put in the forceps, and move it from one side to the other, and it would not come out; then I did not cease to refine and engineer different ways of instruments, until one day I took it with forceps well made, according to its form which will be shown at the end of this chapter, until I drew it out and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the master judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you place your cure on what I do not say, because books cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare with very little great things, and with what is present and lacking, find nine works, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign objects which occur in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the limbs where they are stuck except according to two manners: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and the one that leaves by the place where it enters is an arrow embedded in the flesh, and rarely comes out now.  
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it rots and the opening widens; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce around it with a very fine tool until the flesh around it is enlarged, and then remove it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone near the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: do not remove it at all, but leave it until it becomes level after several days, for if the arrow comes close to there, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not go as far as there, and the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then begin the process of removal. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck like this and cannot come out with force, then administer bandages around it, as I told you; then treat the area until it is healed. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in a place in the body where you cannot see it, then probe it with all your strength; and if you feel it, extract it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then widen the wound until it is large enough; and extract the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow that hold it in place, then remove the flesh that is stuck around it from both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow so that you might extract it more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the flesh around it is rotten, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood is contrary to you, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting a nerve or vein, and put whatever you can to move the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell upon him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do so, then place him according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that has come from another side, where it appears nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place if one can see or feel it apparently: then cut upon it as much as the pincers can grasp and then extract it; if it jumps now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then begin the extraction again until it comes out forcefully; and if there were an arrow in it, push it all the way through; and if it were a bone, and you see that pushing is required, use an instrument with a pointed head so that the point of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument; and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is lifted, push the instrument with the point entering in, to make the extraction easier. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is appropriate. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow strikes or pierces the belly or bladder or side, and it is close, and you can cover over it, do so; and beware of covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it heals. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape: 
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of making them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed end is also like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as here is the shape: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for pushing and pulling is this: 
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one heals, of which there are XVI in the head, namely: II arteries that are behind the ears, which are called the two “herbech”; and the II arteries that are in the II temples, appearing; and II veins that are in the II corners of the II eyes, which are called “aspires”; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the head above the nose; and the II guindeges that are at the neck; and the II veins that are on the lips above the mouth, these are the veins that are called “augeherich”; and II veins that are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly heals are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and common people call it the "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and common people call it the "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side, and common people call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossa, and it is the one from which one heals, which appears manifestly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvation vein is the one which is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the pocket on the left side, and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The cutting of the veins that are behind the ears helps against old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of the bloodletting, as I told you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two hanging folds from the head: hold them with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, it is a sign to cut there; then take the lancet, and put it under the vein down to the bone, then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well two fingerbreadths across, and make blood come out until you see enough; then bandage and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for ancient migraines, and chronic, and habitual ophthalmia, and for a body with sharp tears; and the quality of the bloodletting is as I say: and it is that the patient tightens his neck so that the two veins appear openly; and he feels the thumb under his finger, and then signs to begin; then he lifts the heart above the vein at the top with his index finger, and pushes the lancet underneath, and lifts the vein at the top, and cuts it, as you have done in the other two veins, and let blood flow according to your need; then loosen the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then tie it up, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction, as at the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic for diseases of the face that are old, and for migraine, and for redness. 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then loosen the patient's collar and bind the vein until it is tight and never open it again with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not right that the flame be too strong; and bind it askew, for the bone is nearby, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The binding of the two veins which are in the two temples helps against boils, and tinea, and redness, and inflammation in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their binding is that the patient twists his neck with some cord, as before; then bind it, and let the binding be across, a prick through the length of the flame a prick wide, for there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is delicate, it may break; then make a bandage of cloth soaked in blood, as much as you need, and then tie it with cotton, and bind it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting from the vein at the temple is good for fevers and strong headaches, and for facial diseases such as migraine and redness that appears on the face, even when it is old; and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient squeezes his neck, then he pulls his nose to your left hand, and takes a long delicate flame and sticks it just above the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well easily, and the blood will start running now.  Do not go too far with it; make the blood run according to your need, then tie it up for a night because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sinew of two guindeges helps in the constriction of the urethra, and at the beginning of menstruation, and for many diseases, and for empetigine, and for corrodens, and for herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the sinew is such that the patient draws his neck below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a seat, then he cuts the vein along one piece widely, then draws out the blood temperately, or as much as necessary; then redo it in the other vein, then untie the string, and remove all the veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle; and leave him until morning, so that the wound may heal. 
de la sainie des leivres	Of sinews from hares. 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sinew of the veins of hare's lips above helps for a cold sore in the mouth, and for gum disease, and fissures of the lips, and teeth and throat pain. 
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the vein is to make the patient sit in front of you and pull out their neck as I have said; then turn back the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them because they are black, and because around them there are small black veins: so cut both, and if you do not know them and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and just as well do the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same way. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein below the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein below the tongue helps after the cephalic vein and it is for constriction of the throat and eye diseases and mouth diseases; and the quality of the bleeder is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein: cut both, and do not go too deep, because there are arteries below. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins from which we commonly bleed are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a wide, sharp flame-tempered knife, or with a subtle olive instrument like cutting knives; and they are called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame-tempered knife is very well known, and it is as wide as you see: 
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary for opening the large, full veins containing thick and cloudy blood; and this is the shape of the olive-shaped knife: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and it is for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle, citrine blood. 
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are below the throat, or neck, or chest, or belly; and it behooves the bleeder to bleed moderately, and to be wary of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding comes, then it must be cauterized as I have said; and the flame should not be stabbing but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must extract it and change to another; or if you want none of its vein, or you make a vein in its place on the arm: it opens clearly; and cut with a knife flame as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the vein, then it is fitting that you extract the arm, so that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place with a scratch, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife flame; and beware that you do not strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for that is an artery: wipe it then. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: hasten then and put your finger along its length, and remove your finger if the bleeding stops; for this often happens; then bind up the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move it for the patient; be without fear and do not move it until it is healed.  
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and it comes back to you, and the medicine is not present to you, then bind the artery if it appears, for the head of the retractor; and stop the bleeding. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of a fig tree and cut it, and take one of the halves and tie it on well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, it is good; if not, apply the cure as we have said, with powders which stop blood; and the stopping is not bad in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the bandage on the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle helps it to draw blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the healer to beware of the nerve which is below, and if he points too much with the instrument and finds the nerve, it will swell and the healing will be spoiled, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men because of its subtlety, then you must heal it with an instrument that has been dulled; and avoid the nerve as best you can. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then he should make a long incision. 
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic helps it to draw blood from the head, and aids as well; and it behooves one to heal it by pointing at the flame of olive or myrtle, for it is the safest of all the veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery below. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and do not be troubled if one must attempt the first time, and begin again; and by chance the place swells for some men when one must attempt the first time, but it does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the incision is according to your thought. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is performed only to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses; and whether the bloodletting is done in one of the three veins which are: namely, cephalic, basilic, and median cubital; and it should be done at the beginning of spring for young people, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and it should be done on the first day or the third, after two hours or three. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding that is administered to the sick has no determined hour, but only when need be by day or by night, in all hours and at all times; and it does not suit to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying fruit before the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should one bleed the elderly who have passed sixty years. 
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in any manner that it may be, it is fitting that they cleanse their bowels with a light clyster, if they have retained much phlegm, so that the veins do not draw from the bowels the putrid superfluities harmful to the principal members; nor should one bleed someone who is too full of meats, nor who is drunk, as long as they are intoxicated, nor those who are dropsical; and one should avoid bleeding after colic passions, vomiting, discharge from the belly, and multiplication of seed in women, and exertion, and wakefulness, and fasting, and those who have lost much strength, or by something of war or body; then subdue the humors, if they are gross, by meats and drinks and medicines if you have them; then enter a bath if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the left arm around the third hour as we have said; and keep yourself that day from work, and exertion, and luxury, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow; then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell, and are felt; then moisten the bleeder's knife flame with a drop of old oil, then put your index finger of your left hand below the place one fingerbreadth where you want to bleed, so that the vein does not move when it is cut. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as quickly as strings in a snare, and if some are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it behooves that the bloodletters be advised in these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, begin again a little below that place or above hastily, if the veins are not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the vein is swollen, and the patient faints, leave it for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will come; do not enter a bath, then begin the bloodletting again if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or if you cut subtly with your knife and you doubt that it will not issue as much blood as you see, apply all the flame directly to that opening itself; and work quickly so that the vein is swollen; for this happens often when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the lancing again, and put a poultice of oil on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and the oil in this place makes the poultice; and thus administer the poultice of oil in each vein that you lance, to staunch the flow of blood; and this same does triacle and broth of them, when one puts it on the place; if subtle the blood and it separates when it is too thick. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, even when it is not lanced more than once or twice and the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and put on the place a sponge moistened in water and salt, a hot poultice, and leave it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it remains on the place after several days without any blackness or greenness, do not harm it; and if you see, put on something of aloes or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mustard, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there occurs an abscess and swelling at the incision of the basilica; put then your hand on it, and if you find the place soft under pressure from your hand, that appearance is bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then putting anything of what we have said on it, for you might by chance cut an artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood. 
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, to make a wider incision and let the blood flow freely; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled frequently in small amounts, and it should be done by cutting across, not straight down. This method of bleeding is safe from excessive blood loss and nerve damage and is better than a long or deep cut.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body lacks blood during bleeding, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, before the bleeding he should eat softened bread in thick syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the bleeding, after a lot of blood has been drawn, it is fitting that he inhales broth of meat and subtle aromatic syrup, and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.  
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to have his arms opened and bleed again, it is fitting, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time, according to the amount of his continuing strength. 
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wants to bandage his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong flesh, if he bandages seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour. 
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And he who wants to bleed from another place, he should bleed on the second day or the third. 
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood in the body that has already been heated and causes fever; so it behooves you to draw out a large quantity and widen the opening as much as it bleeds freely; then after you have followed all the conditions of bleeding, put your hand on his pulse while he bleeds so that death does not come instead of blood, and this happens often when the bleeder is negligent; and it is not right when you see him untie his arm and let the blood out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard upon it; nor if it is curved, that he stretches out his arm hastily, for that would be wrong; but leave it as long as it bleeds the second time; or apply the point of a flame to it until the cold blood at the vein's opening comes forth freely, and put a small piece of silk sharpened to a point on it and press lightly.  
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein at the back of the arm is healthier than the vein on the head because it is thicker. 
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of drawing blood is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the pulse is red, then it is tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then the blood is drawn across, not wide nor long; and the opening should be wide, and the blood drawn very close to the joint of the hand; and if none can come out, the hand is put back into hot water and the blood allowed to run into the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back into hot water at all, for it is done more in winter than in summer; and the drawing of blood from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are neither artery nor nerve there. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sinew of the salvation of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one can see it; and if the sinew is sideways, and if you cut it from end to end, it does not grieve anything; and do not go too deep into the flesh, for the nerves are under all naked of skin, and then put the hand in hot water, if the sinew freezes in the wound, and cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and wax on the vein to solder quickly, and do so for each vein. 
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sinew in the left hand is worth for the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have told you about the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The venom of the viper is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the thighs and legs ancient, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its venom is that the patient puts his foot in sharp hot water, and rubs on the vein until it bursts, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and by above the foot there go many reins; therefore heal the larger vein or at the ankle which moves best. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and the healing must traverse as in copying; and let the flames be anesthetized. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the hot water and let the vein empty well. 
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sinews fail the first time, start again a second time above a spot, for the muscle is salty; and do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do the same to the shinbone of the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The muscle of the sciatic vein is at the ankle strong, and its sinew is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for hot blood. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its sinew is such that the patient enters or bathes, and squeezes above the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then squeeze the sinew in all the ways that you can, and by crossing it; and it is worth more that you cut it, for the muscle is underneath, and it is very full of blood for most men. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then squeeze any vein of it that opens or behind the two feet, and toward the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and draw as much blood as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and remove it; it is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping glasses 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horn, or of brass, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done without pricking is done in two ways: either with all fire, or without fire; and cupping which is done by pricking and drawing blood is done on fourteen points of the body, of which one is on top of the head; and the other at the nape of the neck; and two others on both sides of the neck; and a cup under the chin; and cups on both shoulders; and a cup on the buttocks; and cups along both arms; and cups on both legs; and cups on both ankles; and cupping does not draw blood except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it weakens no one, as is done with bleeding from a vein; and it should not be administered, neither with all fire nor without fire, in any illness which comes from repletion, until all the humors are evacuated. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to illness, or by custom, to cup, let us administer them every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and both and in any time; for there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and there are some who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and on their neck, and darkness on them; and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swelling of the tongue, and spit blood; and there are some who dream, and see by night blood and sadness and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and immediately when it is the middle of the month, we order them not to be cupped after three hours of the day. 
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps against the headache... that comes to them, and it is not right that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this cupping is in place of the bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is not right that he who is of cold complexion uses it, or who has diarrhea, for it does them great harm; and for this reason it is not right that old men use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become oblivious, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a bit lower due to the doubt of oblivion. 
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping on the neck is in place of the healing of the head and the basilica, and therefore it is good for constriction of the breast, and for a fissure in the canal of the lung, and all that, and for repletion; and a little should be applied, because if it holds too firmly, it will cause oblivion or stomach or heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the second ribs of the neck is good for headaches, ophthalmia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the healing of the basilica; and you must instruct the patient to press his hand upon it, so that he does not sever the artery, and no flow of blood occurs. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The application of cupping under the chin is good for diseases of the mouth, and for gum disease, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is applied where there are sores on the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is good for diseases that come from heat and swelling. 
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cupping on the elbows is as good as three veins in the arms, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the healer that he does not apply too much force, because the flesh is thin there, and underneath are nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	A cup applied to the buttock is good for hemorrhoids in the fundament and for illnesses beneath it; and it must be that the cup is large, and made of iron, so that it can draw well; and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break and make great wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	If the cupping glasses on the legs bleed openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the loins, and the bladder, and the spleen; and loosen the flowers; and are placed on both thighs, and both ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring on wasting in many conditions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on a cupping glass is that you first put it empty, and then quickly suck up air, and apply it immediately, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and see the redness of the blood; then remove it and replace the cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are some who have tough flesh, and clear pores: so it is good to strike once only, and make wide wounds, and one deep mark; and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it is necessary to cut it twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to cut it a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only make one incision. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we start again often; and if the vein is thick, we pierce it deeply, and the ends are such that the heart is pierced only slightly, and it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and who has few pores, that you moisten the place where the cupping glass will be with oil that is stimulating and dissolving: if it is summer, with violet oil or with sweet almond oil, or with pumpkin seed oil; and if it is winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluousness is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or balsam, or oil of dill, and the like. 
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if he whom one is healing has tender flesh and large pores, it is not fitting to put any oil on, but one must wash him after the cupping with rose water, or cold water, or water of blackberry, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or other like. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise with water of myrtle, or of sumach, and of like things. 
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluousness should rise with old wine, or water of vinegar, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or other like; and it is not fitting to heal with cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and he must not sleep after cupping, and it is fitting that he wash himself when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped.  
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.
