And guard against it if the one who is healing is choleric, and if the wound is too raw and inflamed; then it is fitting that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in season, and similar things; and eat little, and roasted meat, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine half-old, which is between old and new, and eat little, and roasted meat, and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he gets cupped, he should drink more than he eats; and it is fitting to give some men sometimes ginger or musk before cupping, or after, to strengthen the principal limbs; and let the wound be subtle, but it is not fitting for those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Cupping glasses which are placed without wounding are those which are placed on the liver, and on the thigh, and gouty areas, and on the belly and buttocks and loins and hip, for these members do not suffer to be wounded, and we only do it to draw blood from one member to another, just as we place them on the breasts when a newborn is nursing; to remove viscosity which is in a member, such as we place cupping glasses on the belly and buttocks to reduce the member; and to remove pain, when there is obstruction or stone, then by its attractive virtue it removes the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place; and so it does when placed on the liver and thigh when there is retained windiness. These cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this have been boiled. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered by fire is as follows: 
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should be two inches wide and half a palm long, and it has at its side near the middle a small hole, as for putting in a needle; and it should be of horn, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and it has in the middle a crossbar of horn or iron, to put a wick soaked in oil; and they are made in large and small sizes according to the illnesses and the age of those who use them; for cupping glasses for children are different from those for old people, and those for thin people are different from those for fat people. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should put this cupping glass on the limb as follows: take the wick soaked in wax or linen and put it through the crossbar that is in the middle of the cupping glass so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup and does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, with the two points resting on the hole that we have described, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes out, remove the cupping glass; and take the linen as before and start again often, if you need to.  
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered for the illness of pleurisy, to all acute [conditions], it has neither stalk nor hole, and is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb alone; and this is its form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping glasses are not administered except on limbs where one cannot apply cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and on bare parts lacking flesh, such as breast or nose, and other similar ones; and the quality of the user is such that when you find cupping glasses that are in sweet water, clean and without pores, then take them; and put them one night in sweet water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then bleed a vein and apply a cupping glass, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and apply the cupping glasses; and when they are full and draw, if it is a place where one can apply a cupping glass, then apply it, for this is much better afterwards. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, if it lifts the place of ease, and then of sharp, very well, and then it breathes; and if its veins heal too much after the flesh of the wounds, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and put on top until the wound is tightened; and if the veins are multiplied, put ground vitriol, or alum, and similar things, until it is tightened; or you put half of peeled beans on the place, and leave them until they burn on the spot, this will stop now; and if you need more, take other wounds. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not want to take hold, rub the place with fresh blood, or you put a needle in it until the vein comes out, and then you put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn; and when you see that they are falling, powder a bit of aloes and salt crushed, or ash, they will fall now. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fracture and dislocation. 
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the folly of men is cast upon this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor read a letter from them; and for this reason the science is strange in our land, for I have never found any good one; and I know nothing but through the science of the ancient books which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and I have shortened it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are ministered, as I have done in these two chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say or prologue of this book the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding and dwells on truth so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art and teach it to others. 
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the sick person on one side and the other, if nothing else hinders him, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his time is not very favorable, or too cold; and forbid cold meats, that is to say cold dishes, and game and goat meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, or spreading matter to the limb; if the sick person returns to his first government that he was used to. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is fitting that one nourishes the patient with foods that promote thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in broth, rice, and pies, and veal belly, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. 
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For thick nourishment recovers muscles and heals the break more quickly. 
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	Know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot be well set or soldered according to their nature because of the dryness of their limbs, nor can those which are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but have no fear, bind the broken bone with large splints that tighten and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; do not remove them quickly from his work, and for this reason he must be nourished with thick foods, as we have said.  
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways. 
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures. 
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go awry, and others that sharpen, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small crack throughout. 
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own treatment and instrument for restoration, according to what memory comes back into place; and a fracture of the bone is recognized because the limb is twisted and clearly appears deformed when pressed with the hand; and when there is neither twisting nor pain when touched, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it may well have twisting or a crack or a small fracture.  
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not fitting that you move it with your hand, but apply the remedies that will come later, and then extract it now subtly. 
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that for a break that goes into the joint, and where the two parts are separated, it is fitting to now set them straight equally, just as abscesses should come alive; and if a hot abscess comes, leave it alone for a day, until the abscess is calmed; then set it equal to what you can lightly and gently move, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restorations of one who has pieces; then extract it, as it will be fitting later. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the broken bone is in two parts, whether it is the hand or foot, or one small limb at your hand or with two cords or one cord and at your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape so that when the parts of the broken limb are loosened, you soften through all means the additions to their places, moving what you can, and be careful that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and adjust the two ends of the bone well according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right; if it sets straight beautifully, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who cause boils and contraction of the limb by their work, as we have seen many times. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, chastise the patient well so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor on turning, nor in any other way; and be sure to keep the limb so secure that it does not feel any pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not properly set, and you must put it in a different position so that it does not feel any pain; and be careful that it is set straight so that crookedness does not come when it is restored; and the quality of a broken limb is as I have told you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form. 
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and hands and similar ones; so it is fitting to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs; so it is fitting to wrap them with a wide and strong band, for the wide bands embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no gap; then tie around bandages lightly, three turns or four according to the limb, and restrain your hand a little on the whole bandage, then go above the break and restrain it less, so that the break then moves a little away from the break; and soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp a large part of the sound area, then take the other bandage, and turn around again over the broken area; then return to the part below the break, and restrain it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then put between the bandages strips of linen or cloths, until they are all equal, then tie everything over with a bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something soothing to the hot abscess, and that removes the swelling, and leave it like this for several days; then strain on your steles, and they should be half the width of a cane, cut straight, or from wood from which we make wedges, or from palm leaves, and they should be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the stele that we place on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as is appropriate for the limb, whether small or large; then strain on the steles as you did in the first hour, then tie a thread neatly above them, as in the first hour on the fracture; narrower beneath, less so above; and it is necessary that the threads are moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish men who make their bandages with twisted hempen cords, it is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it is not right that there be less than two finger spaces between each stele. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore from the heads of the bones after tightening in their healthy state, then put poultices of linen or shredded wool under them so they do not blanch. 
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the heart is broken, I will tell the cure afterward. 
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not behoove to pull out the bones of all fractured limbs on the first day. 
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it does not behoove to put in bones forcefully before 5 days or 7, or more according to your prudence of a hot abscess appearing; and see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take flour that stays at the sides of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of a plaster restoring the fracture in many positions, and the same for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three abareis and ladani and enule and asefetide and gum arabic and mugat, each ten drachmas; myrrh and aloes, each five drachmas; alechil nine drachmas; and make powder, and mix them with the white of an egg. If the complexion of the man is hot, then use this plaster, for it is a good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth much to many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is worth for torsion: take mugat and vismalve, each ten drachmas; myrrh and aloes, each nine drachmas; acaice six drachmas; bolic armenic ten drachmas; and grind well, and boil with vinegar or the white of an egg, and administer it.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and eases the pain arising, and makes use of the bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and moisten it in lye and boiled oil, and put on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removes the pains. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make a plaster that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make a plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to reduce the remaining inflammation of an abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, one part of each; and grind them, and mix with wine, and if the limb is scalded, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and apply.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make a stronger plaster than the first, when a hard abscess comes for the restoration of the limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take marshmallow roots and flax seeds, plantain, melilot, and sanicle, and violet flowers and chamomile flowers, one part of each; and grind them, and mix with salt water or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except for cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard. 
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one should put on a broken limb, to restore it, dry things somewhat hot, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and goat hairs cut off, or bird feathers, and mallow, and grind them equally, and make a plaster and bind it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then unbind it a little while after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that the bone has moved from its place; if not, do not unbind it for several days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or swelling, then hurry and unbind it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a damp sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool on it, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it for a night, as long as you are sure of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then start the binding again subtly, and a little plaster, and do not pull it too tightly as before; and be subtle until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess boils and reddens and there is pain and swelling, you have removed all of it, and you need to apply plaster and a bandage, if it recurs, as you did first equally. 
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, do not untie it except after III days or IV or V or VII; and never leave it for XX days, according to what you see, as long as the fracture heals, and the adjustment of the flesh above approaches; then restrain it more than before, and make its flesh thicker, as I said before; and if you see the place dry more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; therefore, when you untie it, apply a cloth soaked in warm water, every time, and leave a small opening at the joint; by this work, nourishment then comes to the limb, and quickly amends what the foolish mire has done, which twisted the limb: this is bad, and these are perilous works, and I do not see anything else but to leave it and work it straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking 
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck bone breaks all the bone down to the syfac which is below the bone, as a hatchet or ax does; and for this reason this manner of fracture is called "haichure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone above without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fissure or neck of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things. 
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches up to the membrane that is below the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is large or small. 
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is rejoined to the bone as fine as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and it makes the piece of bone go in, and the veins are cut as the blacksmiths do when they strike on the cauldrons; if the stone goes in. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have soft or wet bones, such as the head of a child; and it happens in all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are detached, like chips; and I will speak about them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the retraction on them, and the inquisition of the tendons, and by the corrupted flesh that is upon them. 
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	Similar hairiness is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs gently upon it, if it appears black fractured. 
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, take care of the patient's accidents, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and pallor, and fever with chills, and the like coming out forcefully and reddening, and other similar things in various dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a dangerous accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.  
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the least that you can. 
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone becomes corrupted, and accidents come as we have said. 
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, it is fitting that you split the fractured part thus: and take the head of the patient securely, and uncover upon the bone in all the ways that you can, and upon the shape of the wound more often than you can; and if discharge of blood comes to discover the bone, or an abscess forms, aid it as is necessary, and fill the place with cloths softened in rose oil; and make the wound rest until the abscess that has formed is appeased, and you are assured of the discharge of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method if is that you cut at a narrow cutting in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another cutting larger than the first. 
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of different sized incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and are made of tempered iron; and in work lightly, so that you do not dull the point. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, thus administering incisions with trepans, not so much that they do not pierce beyond the bone where you are testing, and it must have above the point a margin or a circle, which does not let the point go beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, so that each one comes in its place according to the kind of bone, so that you have trepans for all kinds of bones; and this is the form of the three manners of trepans: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place the trepan on the bone and turn it back and forth until you know the bone is pierced; then place the trepan elsewhere a bit after, and so do all around, then cut with a saw the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pliers; and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the dura mater. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, it is fitting that you leave the instrument which remains attached to the bone with all other instruments similar to a chisel, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other chisel; and if there remain any small bones or scales, remove them lightly with the instruments; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is that which Galien says, which is safer; and he praises it very highly, and this is his word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is fitting first that you uncover a part of the bone where the break appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lentil-shaped chisel, of which this is the form:  
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharpened on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet upon it, so that you lightly chip away at the bone all around, and take good care of the cloth which is underneath; if it is torn by the bone, remove the bone lightly, for one can remove it well without harm and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through to the skin, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, then you should scrape away that roughness and remove the scales with a delicate razor, of which you should have various sizes, in order to administer the most suitable one for each place according to the work and the shape of the fracture. 
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with large razors, and afterwards use smaller ones, and do not cease doing so until it is well. 
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is fitting that you administer care according to its direction; and this is something not easily answered by one who has put his study into this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the syfac is uncovered, then you should take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it upon the wound; then take another cloth doubled into two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and lay it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can so that you do not burden the syfac, then administer a bandage over it, and do not tighten it excessively only enough to hold the wound; and leave it like this for one or two days until the inflammation of the abscess has subsided, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily root, vetch flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder of these things, and sprinkle it on the wound, and administer now cleansing medicines without any biting sensation; and ensure that the wound is now clean, that you do not leave any ointment there, nor allow pus to accumulate, for when pus gathers upon the surface of the brain, it will corrode and constrict, and cause the patient great harm; for when one puts something irritating on the syfac, it will sting above it.  
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt. 
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come except for the medicine that has been placed on it, so that it may have its effect, then it is fitting that you take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and in glue one cloth and put it on the affected area; then cure it in the manner of cures as it is fitting until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts of the nose are rarely broken, or one by itself, for they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it bends or twists, and then heals.  
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is fitting that you put your little finger or thumb on the nose, and place the break inside your index finger, and at the purse by pressing, until the nose returns according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and the bone cannot return to its place, then you must place it equal to the head of a nail, a large point. 
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, you must do the same, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscesses that have formed are calmed, then bind at the head of the knee, bandages of linen. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one to the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the hollows of the knee.  
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must moisten the bandages in butter and change them each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary for them to be softened in a confection of yolk of egg, and mill powder; then leave the bandage on as long as the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.  
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never put goose feathers in place of bandages, and if it comes loose, wrap it again, and hold the break together, and let the patient breathe among them; do what you see. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if boils come to the nose while you are working on it, put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or a poppy seed poultice. 
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if boils do not come, put a plaster made of sesame flour and frankincense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put on light bandages, and do not tie the nose; and if the fracture of the nose is small and it is broken in small pieces, extract it with appropriate instruments for this, then sew up the incision and treat it with things that promote healing and bonding, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with bandages, and put canes of flax, until it heals. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the jawbone 
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below, and there is no wound showing, and the break is below only, and is not broken in two, but forced inward, then the expert can easily recognize it. 
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is fitting, if the break is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left side of the jawbone, put your index finger of the right hand in and push the break inward slightly, and fix it with the other hand by pushing outward, and make it equal. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is in two parts, it is fitting that you administer extension in two parts, so that it is equal. 
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if loosening of the teeth occurs, or breakage, tie them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put cerate on the broken jawbone, and put two cloths over it; and put a large well-made star, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, over the cloths, and tie it up at the temples as you are able, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day and then put back into place what has changed; and apply a plaster made from powder from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour after you have removed the cerate; and put light linen over the plaster. And if the plasters dry out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed; often it is healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, treat them as we have said many times. 
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see that no piece of bone is removed; use subtle instruments suitable for this. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a flame according to your need.  
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, if the wound is large, apply dressings suitable for it to promote flesh until it is healed. 
de la forcele	Of a forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks several times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three ways: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forceps is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put the fracture equal to your needs, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor defect. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, put under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and make it large according to your need; stretch and lift the force, and pull the sphere with your hand so that you set the fracture evenly as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the bone out further because it comes in straight, it is fitting that the patient lie often on his back, and put under the shoulder a medium pillow, and push the ministers the shoulder down until the bone of the humerus is raised. 
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then straighten the fracture according to your skill, and if you find it shattered, it is fitting that you split it up; and draw the pieces lightly together, and if the bone cannot join for any pressure, apply one of the incisors that you have; but place under the humerus this instrument to keep it in place. 
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and it should be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, soak a cloth in rose oil and assafetida and wine, and apply it. 
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of a bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone a plaster of mill flour and egg yolk, and put light wadding on top, and put a splint under the armpit, if you need it; then take a very large bandage a palm wide, then put the cloth double on the wadding and the plaster; then take a slender stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage up onto the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit; and loosen it from each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture properly, and you see clearly that the stick does not move on the broken bone, then leave it for a day, and when the bandages slacken, tighten them again; and let the patient lie on his back, and put under his armpit a small pillow when he sleeps to raise the shoulder high up; this will lighten the fracture from the weight of the shoulder, or you tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, for twenty days; then start the plaster again, if you see that he needs it, and remove it and leave him like that, until he is restored; and it is restored at most in twenty-eight days, and less in some men.  
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder 
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks or is out of place by a great distance, and it is not known except by touch; if you set it according to the shape of the break and reset it according to its natural form in all ways as you can; then put on the place powder from a mill with plenty of egg white and light bandages, and put a double cloth on top; then put a wide and delicate splint, a little larger than the shoulder, and if below the splint there are hairs anywhere on the shoulder, use those hairs for bandages of flax so that the splint lies evenly; and then bind it all with a large bandage firmly so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the binding every day; and every time it loosens, bind it again, and set the splint straight if it is out of place, and lay the patient on their side; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty days or twenty-five. And when this number is reached, unbind it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that is put back lightly.  
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward and not below the heart, then lift it up and the bone-setter should do what we have said in the fracture of the clavicle to soothe the abscess with heat. 
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot 
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is rarely broken in the middle, but it does happen sometimes; but it often breaks at the ankle. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it sinks downwards, and the patient experiences great pain, shortness of breath, and vomiting, and sometimes the hair stands on end in the broken bone, and they know very well that it is broken. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back and puts a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders and assembles the ribs of the two sides with their hands, and subtly puts them equal in all the ways they can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put plasters and bandages over the broken bone with a subtle plaster of salt or other light herb, and wrap it in a cloth and tie it onto the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the bandage round the back and tighten it evenly, and check every hour if the bandage is loose, and if it is, tighten it; and if it is necessary to untie it due to corrosion or itching that comes to the area, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, remove the plaster, and treat what has come about in a manner of cures; then apply the plaster and untie it when it is healed.  
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs 
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs only occurs in their thickness behind the back, and mainly inside, and they only break because they are slippery; and one feels it well upon inquiry.  
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the break straight, as it should be. 
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster and remove it with a splint, if you need to. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the broken rib is sloping inward, the patient feels great pain and shortness of breath, as well as pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lung; and the patient coughs up blood tinged with pus, and vomits a lot of blood, and this is a serious ailment, and the ancients have said it is a grave affliction. 
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is fitting to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to push the break outward. 
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, so that hot abscesses do not come, if they have not already come. 
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, we heal it. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that we place cupping glasses on the spot to suck out humors, and it seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass may draw superfluities to the spot because of weakness. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that we should cover the spot with wool moistened in hot oil, and place bandages between the ribs to make the binding even, then it is treated with a poultice of pleurisy root, meat, and medicine. 
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot suffer because of the bone pointing through the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut open above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument under it to guard the nerve; and then one should carve the bone, and draw lightly on it, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put it on cloths softened in rose oil, and place them on the spot; and care for it as long as is necessary for the abscess, and let it lie often on the side where it should be, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of a broken neck 
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture of the bones in the neck, and it happens that it rains; and also in the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortally wounded in several ways, and if he moves them and feels well when they are stretched and pricked, know that the juncture of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if care is given to him.  
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know whether it is healthy or not, see if its feet are softened, and if the accidents that are in the hands are softened, and on the back there comes flatulence and excretion without volition; and when one has turned it on its stomach, there comes excretion without volition. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned on his back and wants to rise, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal; if one does not labor in its cure. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, the thing is lighter.  
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is such that you consider whether there is a hot abscess; if so, put rose oil or oil of egg yolk on the spine until it is soothed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and order the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is healed.  
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover it on the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment containing charcoal, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," put your left hand in your pocket, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then apply the plaster and the splint on top, if you need them; then remove it, and if there are broken bones, do as above, and remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone  
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there would only be a slight decrease in stature; and after a long time, and leaning to one side, pain comes to the patient at the location, and tenderness, and swelling where the break is. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above, as long as you are above the fracture; and know which is the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is in the head only, then make that fracture equal, as long as it is in its natural shape. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach, as long as the restoration of that fracture appears to you. 
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it equal, put a plaster on it, then put a splint of wood or horn on top, and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the area below the ribs, as long as the ligament is equal. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess should come, do not touch it until the abscess is soothed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and that is the way.  
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	from the breaking of the shoulder 
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of two methods: one of which is that you take a splint of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two cords and lift them up, and lay the patient down on a seat; then place the splinted arm broken upon the splint so that it reaches the armpit, and make a curve in the splint, then lift it up onto some heavy object or have assistants stretch it out downwards; then put your hands on the break, aligning it with both hands together, until the break returns as it should.
