Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you place the patient on his mattress and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants that one hold what is above the break with his hands, and the other hold below at all of the limb, and each stretch in his own direction.  
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants to their respective roles. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is fitting that you place one ligature midway below the armpit, and the other toward the elbow, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is toward the elbow, it is fitting to put the ligature gently, without effort, as long as the fracture is aligned on the side and on the elbow; then set the fracture evenly, as it should be, and extract it, if no abscess arises. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess arises, do not extract it for seven days, and put moistened linen soaked in vinegar and rose oil on it until the abscess is calmed; then extract it, and the manner of extracting it is that you place a plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder support, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and put on the sheet, and extract upwards on the shoulder support, and on the arm so that the arm is in its proper place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints and place a larger and stronger splint on the fracture than the others, and have two finger widths of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends three finger widths on each side; then strain upwards on the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less remotely. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seating of the splints and the constriction as we have said in the hour that you are restoring the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess heat, then leave it bound until the seventh day as we have said; then look at the bandage every three days, so that itching does not swell or come to the place where the constrictions cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.  
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you hold it as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents comes, do not untie it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of equal wool, and look every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or is not loosened by the ties; if it heals by the virtue of medicine, give him the meat as we have previously said, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be large. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be held for forty days in all; and then he must untie them and administer baths and ointments to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and congested, it will remain loosened for I day or II months. 
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm 
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "focills," of which one is small, and is the one that goes into the pouch; and the other is large, and is the one that is below, towards the little finger; by chance it breaks the large focus alone, or the small one, and by chance both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small focills are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, it is a bad healing, and more grievous than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small focus alone that is broken, then you must lightly extend it and put it equal. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone, then it is necessary to restrain more strongly; and extend it upon a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little toes lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher up so that the patient does not suffer any hardship; then extend the minister's arm below his hand, or at the bandage, and another minister above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal, according to its best shape. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is none detached that you can grasp with the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision over the bone, as we have said before. 
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a singular chapter; then take the care.  
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration boils appear, then apply a poultice made of rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and bind it subtly on top until the boils subside. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cerote and apply a plaster of mill powder with plenty of egg yolk, then place the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be stronger now and a bit wider than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones or two; and pull more above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths over the fracture be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is pulled be linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And watch over the limb and the ligament after some days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you bathe the limb with hot water, until the itching is soothed; and let the limb not be tightly bound. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the binding, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones are loosened, and similar things, so address it. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care so that nourishments cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, it is necessary that you loosen it a bit and leave it like that for some days, until nourishment goes to it, and then remove it. 
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, do not unbind him until 20 days.  
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Where there is a sprain, then he can put his hands on his neck, and let his necks be equal, and guard against movement and swaying, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and by chance in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand 
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have two there occur few fractures, and it comes but more often a pain. 
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or pained, it behooves that the patient sit crosswise, and sit straight in front of him equally; then put his hand on a cloth stretched out, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and put them equal to the pointers, as long as they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place; and it is wrapped in one sheet of linen. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the pardedens around the belly of the plant, make a sphere of bandages, and instruct the patient to squeeze it at his fractured plant; then bind it with a long bandage, and let the star be as large as the palm of the hand, and pull it out, as it should be. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the defuer, it is fitting that you put a star above and another below on the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then bind it tight around the hand and seal the bond between the two. 
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the bones of the two fingers, if it is the thumb, put it equal, as it should be; and pull it out with the plant, and if you see fit, put a small straight star to lift the fracture, and do not move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, as in the index finger or one of the others, put it equal, and bind it with the healthy finger that is next to it; or bind them all in an I shape, so that they do not move, or put a star on it, as on the thumb; and take care in the restoration and in the disposition of a hot abscess, and help those who come to you, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh 
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one sees it well when it turns in front and behind; and its restoration is done by tying one ligature above the break and another below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends their ligature to their respective side equally; and this is when the break is between the bones. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, one of the ligatures should be towards the buttock, and the other ligatures below the break. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then the ligatures should be placed near the knee, and the extension below; then set the bones equal with both hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, if abscesses appear anywhere. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down then return to your work and your treatment; the ligature is made in this manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap on the fracture I bandage hard doubled in II or III, and leave the superfluity, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put I long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee underneath, and bring the head of the thread above; then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then place on the fracture splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then apply the eighth place between the leg and the thigh of cloths soft to make equal the tightness, then begin to tie three twists or four on the fracture; and when going further above the fracture, the tighter it becomes; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you put between the leg and the thigh, and tie III splints that are above, then return below to the head of the thread, as far as you come to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus until there comes neither abscess nor swelling nor any other resemblance.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, so that the limb is dislocated, and straightened as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that stick out, then you must extract them, if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut into the place and pull with force; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken so that one puts splints on it, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in this restoration thus made does not make the patient lame. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 40 days or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions. 
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the path from the knee 
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the path from the knee there are few breaks, but it bends many times.  
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is only a crack or a hole, and occurs in any wound, and without a wound, then it is good. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts together what is broken to its due place, as much as it can be assembled and moved; then apply a plaster, and put a round splint on top, if you need it, and remove it as necessary, then observe all the provisions we have mentioned for other fractures, such as abscesses, cautery, and other similar things; so apply to each accident what is fitting until it is healed. 
de la brisure de la jambe	of a broken leg  
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by right name "tibia," and the other is called "fibula"; and all other fractures occur as they do in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as that of the arm, equally, and the work is altogether like. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn them forward. 
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain and it is seen well; and turn it down below.  
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension and set it equal, and tie the splints equally; but however, if the break is bad and there are many pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and adjust it according to your skill. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two bandages of willow wood that are long enough to cover the leg from one side to the other, and let them be twice as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap them around with two bandages above and below, and tie them in the middle, so that the leg cannot lean to the right or left, and thus it is well; and no one should apply any splints along the length of the leg, and if they are made of wood, and put on the leg to prevent movement, and properly done in the fracture or where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is a hot abscess or any other accident; then care for it until it is healed. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones of the foot 
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there does not come a fracture, but the bones of the foot sometimes come to fracture and it is necessary to know and there are not many situations. 
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are fractured, and you see these bones rise on top of each other, have the patient put their foot on the ground as if they wanted to walk, and then place your foot upon theirs where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then apply a plaster and bandages over it, and place beneath the sole of the foot a small board with two fingers thick, and then straighten the foot carefully so that when you have wrapped it in cloths and other things which you need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal whether they are broken or dislocated. 
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, if you restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and it should be a finger wider, then put under the foot that table which I have said, and bind it carefully; and if there are two or three, or more, bones broken, put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the table underneath the foot; and let it be placed on the top of the table above the belly of the foot so that it holds it well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have said; and help each accident as it should be done. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone in the wrist  
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, if you make her sit enlarged, then incline her to the back part, and have her held from behind; then fill the woman's nature with cotton, and put in as much as I stick; then unbend the woman, and lift the back little by little, and then the cotton will jump, as much as it comes to the entrance of the nature, and the bone will return with the stick; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for VII days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of kid, and tie a cane to the hole, and push the whole bladder into the nature; then blow into the cane gently, until the bladder is inflated inside: the nature will return the fracture; then fill with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the arm of a man or woman is broken, if it is set as we have said in the bone of the thigh; and these close fractures are not hidden from those who put their study and experience into this, and understand my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in several positions the right way of restoration: so understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert it into the penis; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will quickly heal. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound 
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It behooves one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, as in the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to have it healed now, so that the healings that we have spoken of testify to this.  
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, if you have no other option, then begin again to restore the fracture in that same hour or day, so long as pus does not come. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus does come, then leave the restoration until a new day, until the pus is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause bad accidents. 
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the heart uncovered, then it is fitting that you put it in place lightly with your hands, with slight extension. 
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear to you to put it equal with your hands, then have this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary for the user that he engrave three or four, according to what he may need in each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and have a large hole so that it does not bend at compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front and thick from the middle forward like this: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called “palainche,” for which reason the curved head must be placed upon the head of the exposed bone; and the end at once, as much as it returns, and be equalized one against the other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone so that the instruments have power. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then cut with an instrument suitable for this, either an incisor or a saw, at your power; then scrape away what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you have set it back in place, then moisten the bandage with black stiptic wine and apply it cleanly; and if it is summer, do not put any cerate or anything else on the wound where there is oil, lest it cause decay and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many a foolish barber has done this and has caused death or corruption upon the patient at times; and let the ligatures be looser and softer than for other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is large or bad, and you fear that evil accidents may come as we have said, and you find pain in the place, it is not right to put on splints; but wrap tightly around, instead of splints, hard bandages, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is beginning to heal, remove what you have put on it altogether and apply healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones. 
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is joined and healed. 
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limb be bandaged in such a way that the wound drains slightly downwards. 
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes and it cannot heal but the wound opens again, know that there are small bone fragments, for which reason you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose fragments that cause the pain. 
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the site, or some other manner of corruption, it is fitting that you treat it according to what is said in the chapter before this one. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not pull it, for often death comes, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a sorry sight to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed then if the swelling is fresh: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg white or with oil; and put them on the swelling in compresses, and bind it well, and do not untie it for three days; and then untie it, and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you bind it on a piece of lead well made; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut it above, and remove the superfluity that appears; or you shave it with any razor until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb which is weak after healing 
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and the limb remains weak and thin afterward, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not come to the limb; or because of a multitude of movements; or because of too great movements, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, therefore he is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and soften the body, until the blood is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and give him joy and leisure; then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch draws nourishment to it, and warm it often with hot water, until nourishment reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural shape.  
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb twisted after the health 
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is exposed, and the form of the limb is unsightly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb all over again, for many foolish men have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and great evils come from it, and perhaps death; nevertheless, if the nodules and the torture are fresh, it is fitting that they be softened with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as diachylon well made, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with grease of goose or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or take fat figs, and crush them with bran of wheat, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling. 
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation removed by continual and prolonged rubbing with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then one must cut up to the bone, with a subtle incisor lightly; and put caution and study into the treatment. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and injury. 
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation comes to someone, if it must now be brought back without delay. 
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the flesh swells, and by chance if one puts it back in place; therefore, one must not move it when it is swollen: many times it causes spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient well then let him be, until the abscess has been quieted; then raise the limb with sharp heat and oil, then soften it lightly, and treat each limb as the treatment will come to its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head down to the feet. 
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It can happen that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are a little loosened from their places, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the feet, and spill the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it returns by itself through several arrangements. 
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and finished, you must reset it quickly and do not delay; and in such a manner that the assistants hold the head of the patient, and put their thumbs into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of both sides; and the other hand should be free, to place equally; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he looks at the wound as evenly as possible, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if resetting it is difficult, even when the two jawbones are together, apply a mixture of hot water and oil, until they soften slightly; do not hesitate to reset it, as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, put soft cloths soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind them with linen; let the patient sleep on his back, with his head resting between two cushions so that he does not move it either to the right or left, nor strain to chew but take light food, as long as the pains are gone and the jawbones are joined; then eat whatever he wants lightly, and do not bother to open his mouth wide for eating and drinking, as long as the mandible is well joined and healed.  
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not converted to their places, then fever and accustomed sweats come, and perhaps loosening of the belly, and perhaps vomiting of bile. 
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction; and many times death comes to those to whom it happens, in nine days. 
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot dislocate both sides within the continuation of it and the foot, and it is dislocated sometimes at the beginning, and one feels it well. 
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms; and then presses the place formed with your palm, and it will return; then put plaster on it and bandage it, and remove it; and the head which is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates sometimes, then you must reset it in its place, as we have said; then put plaster on it and bandage it, and remove it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way, the head of the shoulder is brought back when it is detached from its place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one is that it dislocates at the part of the axle below; and the second is at the part of the buttock; and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the axle, especially in those who have little flesh, for in them it is quickly hastened; in those who have enough flesh, it is hard to hasten, and it returns with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they have a concussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.  
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary then that you test it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that a shoulder is dislocated when it is lowered toward the axle, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest diversity between them; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the axle at the touch the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bone; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its nest, nor move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upward, unless it is hidden, because you will find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not very difficult to reset, when it is new, or when the infant is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is for the minister to lift the patient's hand upward, then place his fingers below the axle, and lift the joint forcefully upward into its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upward, then puts it below; it will come quickly. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days afterwards, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and let him be given a softening and soothing dressing, such as a decoction of alt, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and let it be administered; then let the patient be laid on his back, and put under the armpit a cloth of wool equal, not too soft nor too hard, then put the foot of the bed under the heel of the patient, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister hold the head of the patient so that it does not move down; this shoulder will return now, and if you see that you reset according to this manner: and it is necessary that you have a man present who is larger than the patient; and he be straight towards the side, and put his shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit up so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient down towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, you can put something heavy on them, and the dislocation will return immediately. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is also done in another way: and it is one puts a long burning ember into the earth, whose head should be as round as a pestle, and not too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but let him have cloths soft above, and the patient shall be lying along the length of the wood; then his hand is stretched out on the other side straight, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not wish to return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take an ember of two arms in length and four fingers wide, which has a round head to enter perfectly under the armpit according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie cloths on the head of the wood below so that the wood does not burn the patient, then put it under the armpit of the patient; and extend his arm along the wood, and tie the shoulder onto the wood, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on the rung of a wide ladder, and extend the hand down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.  
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever way it may be, it behoves you to put under the armpit a sphere of equal wool, then put the plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and yolk of egg, upon all the shoulder and around, then strain it under the armpit carefully, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus. 
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it behoves him to rest a little, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then rest more after 5 days or 7, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come upon it, or for another reason, it behoves you to administer cauteries to 3 holes, as it is laid down in the chapter on cauteries.  
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it comes undone after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation which is near the buttock and the breasts or behind, is done by thrusting and extending the arms, and administering it elsewhere; and cure as long as he is healthy. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness to the limb, and slowness in movement, then have the patient bathe many times until that stiffness is relieved and it returns to its original nature. 
de la dislocation dou coute	of dislocation from the rib
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at points, and at points it returns; and if it is dislocated on all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation is not fixed, for one can see it well and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick knife with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is raised, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in the same way as if abscesses were to come, for if abscesses were to come, it would be harmful to return it; and by chance it cannot be returned at all, even when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance death comes. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such, when it can be returned as it is, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and his arms should be spread, and the hands turned according to the knife around, above and below, and push the joint at its ends together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he bends his hand toward his hand, and presses on the root of the palm or the costal which has been dislocated. 
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and let the minister who extends the arm, hold it, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double-length and wide cloth around it; and when the minister reaches the joint, apply oil to the joint to soften it, then push the joint straight, until it returns to its place; and when it is in its place, put dry plaster on it with egg white, bind it tightly, and hang the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not quite right, start the plaster and bandage again, and leave it like that for several days, until it is firmly in place; then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or you put a greasy sheep's fleece on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then bone-set it, and let him enter a bath; and when he sweats, if he rubs the joint moderately, then put the fleece back on, and then enter a bath; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see, then put moist, heated cow dung with butter on it, and strain it on; it will return to its position. 
li dislocation de la main	Hand dislocation 
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is easy, more so than the other joints. Nonetheless, it should be hastily reset in the same hour that it is dislocated, even if the flesh is swollen or an abscess appears hot. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the repositioning is such that you place the affected hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and look at him to make it even, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes as much as it returns Wholeway. It is necessary that you look whether it is well in place; then put the patient's back of his hand on a table for extension and repositioning. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, put the patient's back of his hand on the table, and the minister puts his hand on that appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good. If not, he strains soothing plasters for abscesses socks and leaves it thus without restarting. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it in place after several days, the joint remains crooked; and do not harm the patient further than that as long as the hand is weak, and cannot strain anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; there is no other remedy than to extract by cautery in this case, and perhaps nothing else will work.  
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it like that. 
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is some pain, apply hot water and rub it until it is healed. 
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of fingers 
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then extend the finger and push the dislocation with your thumbs until it returns, then support the head of the finger and bend it toward the part where it is separated; and leave it for two days, and then put it straight that day; and bind it at night, as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this often until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you did before until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in another place.  
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	about the loosening of the shoulder blade from the back 
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade from the back or the neck is dislocated, if there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient. 
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the limbs jump forcefully without volition, and he cannot hold them, and often some members are softened, either both thighs or both arms or one. And often the shoulder blade moves in four parts; the one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez"; the cure is that you consider if the gilbositez came from childhood: if there is no cure or healing altogether. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And the one that comes from falling or blows or similar things, they say ancient manners of cures in many words, which are not very profitable overall; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gibbosity that comes to the breast beforehand, none has neither sense nor feeling; and also that which comes straight on both sides, and one cannot cure except that properly which comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in an equal place, and have a strain below him so that he does not get hurt; then put a coal at the head into the ground, and the other at the feet, and tie a string under the buttocks of the sick person, and the other at the haunches, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers know the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two coals; and they are well closed, the coal as we have said, and the minister puts his palms on the spine into the ground, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board three arms long and put the end under the armpit, and have the patient lie on his side, and push the head of the board under the armpit, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the patient place his feet on the other end of the board, and press hard until it returns to its place; and if you see it, do it with a tourniquet that twists at hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And have two tinders placed at the head of the patient one arm's length apart and two others towards the feet; and between each tinder, above and below, leave a palm's length of space; and in each tinder make one hole where the tourniquet passes, and firmly set the tinders in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of tinders place a turning tinder from which the linen turns; and have two small tinders a palm long on the two turners to turn the tourniquet; then tie the linen among the axles to the tourniquet towards the head, and the other linen towards the feet to the other tourniquet; and let each of the assistants turn his tourniquet along the entire length of the linen, and the master place the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are equal, put a drying plaster on top with plenty of egg, then the bandages, and then the splint from a tablet three finger-lengths long, which covers the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine that is healthy; then tie it with a ligature, as we have said, and use the patient with subtle nourishment until he is healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, you must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have mentioned before; and sometimes administer a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes on the back spine of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation; but it is the bone that appears, for which one should not presume at all: by chance death would come. 
des dislocations de la hainche	Of hip dislocations 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come loose through dislocations alone, and not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and in front and behind; and more often inside than otherwise, and rarely dislocated in front and behind. 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.
