The knowledge of this dislocation inside is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee; and there is swelling behind which feels like a hot abscess because the head of the thigh comes there.  
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one in whom it goes outwards is that this condition is the opposite of those in front. 
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one in whom it occurs in front are that their leg is well aligned according to its structure; however, they cannot bend their knee without pain, and if you try to make them walk, they cannot go forward, and they retain their urine, and their groin swells, and when they walk, they pass on their heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has it behind are that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs. 
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resetting of this kind of dislocation is such that you consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its placement, then there is no cure; and it is not fitting that he should have presumption. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for him whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to return the joint, and stretch it in and out, and move it to right and left; by chance it will return, and does not need another cure. 
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, it is fitting that you prepare a strong minister, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or with a ligature which is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand upon it in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then he binds it tightly with a strong ligature on the thigh; and another holds the head of the ligature; and they extend upward and downward all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.  
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good. 
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must apply treatment according to its resemblance. When the dislocation is in the hip, you should place the patient on his healthy side, then put the bandage on the root of the thigh, and the place below the angle, then extend the bandage upward toward the angle and toward the groin; then have another assistant hold the patient's arms, and embrace the thick part of the injured thigh, and extend it outward in a straight form; it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.  
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner as we have said, it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage above on the two heels, and on the two knees, and let the injured leg be extended two fists more than the others; then hang him by the head from a beam, and let him be suspended so that his arms are outstretched two arm's lengths from the ground; then command one assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and have another assistant hanging with the patient embrace the thigh straight, for the joint will now return quickly. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the leg, have the patient lie down as we said for the one who has gout, and bind a bandage properly on the diseased leg and on the foot as well; then put two embers, one at the head and the other at the feet, then place one ember between the thighs of the patient so that it forms a triangle; and place cloths dampened with water around it so it doesn't burn the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and have the one who is looking hold the dislocation evenly with his hand. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on a table and press as we said for gout, and have the patient lie down on their healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and let the one who is looking place his pain on the diseased angle, then press with the other hand, and extend it down towards the knee. 
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is backward, it is not right to extend the patient downward, nor to raise him up on the ground, but he should be as if his hip were dislocated backward, as we have said about lying on both hips; and he should be on his face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and you must press on the joint at the table; and it will be right when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal; then adjust the thighs, and put plaster on it, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and he rests for three days or four, then unbind him, and put plaster on it; and if you see that they are equal, bind it as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and let him walk well, as long as the limb is comfortable. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee 
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not straighten at his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you have the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee so they form a right angle; and another minister extends his foot, as long as the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he straightens his leg at his thigh easily; and put the plaster on, and allow the leg to be aired at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three days or four, then unbind it; and let the patient not bother walking, as long as the limb is comfortable. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all present, administer strong extension as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed. 
de la dislocation dou talon	of dislocation of the heel 
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes dislocated, and sometimes fully dislocated, both internally and externally.  
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tense in front of the part where it is dislocated; the resetting is gentle, and one must gently extend it with their hands when it is only slightly dislocated.  
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, you must have the patient sit straight, and hold them firmly by the leg, above the ankle; then draw the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards, and push the foot up nicely; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a strong stake firmly in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around it so that it does not hurt the patient; then hold the thigh with one assistant, and another assistant extend the foot with their hands or with a rope, which they tie around the ankle; then both assistants extend evenly, and the stake should be firmly between the patient's thighs to hold them down when extending; then place your hands equally on the dislocation, and have another assistant hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.  
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set right, put the plaster and bandages on top, and bind them tight, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch over the nerves which are above the ankle behind so that the binding is not too tight; then leave it for two days or three, and if the bandage loosens, tighten it; then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess should come, it is fitting that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed. 
des dois	of the two 
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, they must be nicely extended without exertion, and this is an easy thing.  
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, it is fitting that you make the patient sit on a level place or on a table straight up, and put your foot on what appears of these joints, then press your foot firmly until it returns; and when it is equalized, and nothing appears, put under the sole of the foot a table with two legs, then bind it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and make him rest, as long as he is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together 
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and you want to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it long, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, do not be bold; and use at the beginning soothing things for a hot abscess, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess may come alive; and when the limb is in its place, then administer soothing things for a hot abscess, and cure the wound as it is necessary, with drying ointments; and if there is a break with the dislocation, and small bones are broken off, remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for this is worth more according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body. 
Amen	So be it
